# The Second Book of Nephi

An account of the death of Lehi. Nephi’s brethren rebel against him. The Lord warns Nephi to depart into the wilderness. His journeyings in the wilderness, and so forth.

Chapter 1

Lehi prophesies of a land of liberty—His seed will be scattered and smitten if they reject the Holy One of Israel—He exhorts his sons to put on the armor of righteousness. About 588–570 B.C.

1 And now it came to pass that after I, Nephi, had made an end of teaching my brethren, our [afather](#note1a), Lehi, also spake many things unto them, and rehearsed unto them, how great things the Lord had done for them in bringing them out of the land of Jerusalem.

2 And he spake unto them concerning their [arebellions](#note2a) upon the waters, and the mercies of God in sparing their lives, that they were not swallowed up in the sea.

3 And he also spake unto them concerning the land of promise, which they had obtained—how [amerciful](#note3a) the Lord had been in [bwarning](#note3b) us that we should flee out of the land of Jerusalem.

4 For, behold, said he, I have [aseen](#note4a) a [bvision](#note4b), in which I know that [cJerusalem](#note4c) is [ddestroyed](#note4d); and had we remained in Jerusalem we should also have [eperished](#note4e).

5 But, said he, notwithstanding our afflictions, we have obtained a [aland of promise](#note5a), a land which is [bchoice](#note5b) above all other lands; a land which the Lord God hath [ccovenanted](#note5c) with me should be a land for the inheritance of my seed. Yea, the Lord hath [dcovenanted](#note5d) this land unto me, and to my children forever, and also all those who should be [eled](#note5e) out of other countries by the hand of the Lord.

6 Wherefore, I, Lehi, prophesy according to the workings of the Spirit which is in me, that there shall [anone](#note6a) come into this land save they shall be brought by the hand of the Lord.

7 Wherefore, this [aland](#note7a) is consecrated unto him whom he shall bring. And if it so be that they shall serve him according to the commandments which he hath given, it shall be a land of [bliberty](#note7b) unto them; wherefore, they shall never be brought down into captivity; if so, it shall be because of iniquity; for if iniquity shall abound [ccursed](#note7c) shall be the land for their sakes, but unto the righteous it shall be blessed forever.

8 And behold, it is wisdom that this land should be [akept](#note8a) as yet from the knowledge of other [bnations](#note8b); for behold, many nations would overrun the land, that there would be no place for an inheritance.

9 Wherefore, I, Lehi, have obtained a [apromise](#note9a), that [binasmuch](#note9b) as those whom the Lord God shall bring out of the land of Jerusalem shall keep his commandments, they shall [cprosper](#note9c) upon the face of this land; and they shall be kept from all other nations, that they may possess this land unto themselves. And if it so be that they shall [dkeep](#note9d) his commandments they shall be blessed upon the face of this land, and there shall be none to molest them, nor to take away the land of their [einheritance](#note9e); and they shall dwell safely forever.

10 But behold, when the time cometh that they shall dwindle in [aunbelief](#note10a), after they have received so great blessings from the hand of the Lord—having a knowledge of the creation of the earth, and all men, knowing the great and marvelous works of the Lord from the creation of the world; having power given them to do all things by faith; having all the commandments from the beginning, and having been brought by his infinite goodness into this precious land of promise—behold, I say, if the day shall come that they will reject the Holy One of Israel, the true [bMessiah](#note10b), their Redeemer and their God, behold, the judgments of him that is [cjust](#note10c) shall rest upon them.

11 Yea, he will bring [aother nations](#note11a) unto them, and he will give unto them power, and he will take away from them the lands of their possessions, and he will cause them to be [bscattered](#note11b) and smitten.

12 Yea, as one generation passeth to another there shall be [abloodsheds](#note12a), and great visitations among them; wherefore, my sons, I would that ye would remember; yea, I would that ye would hearken unto my words.

13 O that ye would awake; awake from a deep [asleep](#note13a), yea, even from the sleep of [bhell](#note13b), and shake off the awful [cchains](#note13c) by which ye are bound, which are the chains which bind the children of men, that they are carried away captive down to the eternal [dgulf](#note13d) of misery and woe.

14 Awake! and arise from the dust, and hear the words of a trembling [aparent](#note14a), whose limbs ye must soon lay down in the cold and silent [bgrave](#note14b), from whence no traveler can [creturn](#note14c); a few more [ddays](#note14d) and I go the [eway](#note14e) of all the earth.

15 But behold, the Lord hath [aredeemed](#note15a) my soul from hell; I have beheld his [bglory](#note15b), and I am encircled about eternally in the [carms](#note15c) of his [dlove](#note15d).

16 And I desire that ye should remember to observe the [astatutes](#note16a) and the judgments of the Lord; behold, this hath been the anxiety of my soul from the beginning.

17 My heart hath been weighed down with sorrow from time to time, for I have feared, lest for the hardness of your hearts the Lord your God should come out in the fulness of his [awrath](#note17a) upon you, that ye be [bcut off](#note17b) and destroyed forever;

18 Or, that a [acursing](#note18a) should come upon you for the space of [bmany generations](#note18b); and ye are visited by sword, and by famine, and are hated, and are led according to the will and captivity of the [cdevil](#note18c).

19 O my sons, that these things might not come upon you, but that ye might be a choice and a [afavored](#note19a) people of the Lord. But behold, his will be done; for his [bways](#note19b) are righteousness forever.

20 And he hath said that: [aInasmuch](#note20a) as ye shall keep my [bcommandments](#note20b) ye shall [cprosper](#note20c) in the land; but inasmuch as ye will not keep my commandments ye shall be cut off from my presence.

21 And now that my soul might have joy in you, and that my heart might leave this world with gladness because of you, that I might not be brought down with grief and sorrow to the grave, arise from the dust, my sons, and be [amen](#note21a), and be determined in [bone](#note21b) mind and in one heart, united in all things, that ye may not come down into captivity;

22 That ye may not be [acursed](#note22a) with a sore cursing; and also, that ye may not incur the displeasure of a [bjust](#note22b) God upon you, unto the destruction, yea, the eternal destruction of both soul and body.

23 Awake, my sons; put on the armor of [arighteousness](#note23a). Shake off the [bchains](#note23b) with which ye are bound, and come forth out of obscurity, and arise from the dust.

24 Rebel no more against your brother, whose views have been [aglorious](#note24a), and who hath kept the commandments from the time that we left Jerusalem; and who hath been an instrument in the hands of God, in bringing us forth into the land of promise; for were it not for him, we must have perished with [bhunger](#note24b) in the wilderness; nevertheless, ye sought to [ctake away](#note24c) his life; yea, and he hath suffered much sorrow because of you.

25 And I exceedingly fear and tremble because of you, lest he shall suffer again; for behold, ye have [aaccused](#note25a) him that he sought power and [bauthority](#note25b) over you; but I know that he hath not sought for power nor authority over you, but he hath sought the glory of God, and your own eternal welfare.

26 And ye have murmured because he hath been plain unto you. Ye say that he hath used [asharpness](#note26a); ye say that he hath been angry with you; but behold, his [bsharpness](#note26b) was the sharpness of the power of the word of God, which was in him; and that which ye call anger was the truth, according to that which is in God, which he could not restrain, manifesting boldly concerning your iniquities.

27 And it must needs be that the [apower](#note27a) of God must be with him, even unto his commanding you that ye must obey. But behold, it was not he, but it was the [bSpirit](#note27b) of the Lord which was in him, which [copened](#note27c) his mouth to utterance that he could not shut it.

28 And now my son, Laman, and also Lemuel and Sam, and also my sons who are the sons of Ishmael, behold, if ye will hearken unto the voice of Nephi ye shall not perish. And if ye will hearken unto him I leave unto you a [ablessing](#note28a), yea, even my first blessing.

29 But if ye will not hearken unto him I take away my [afirst](#note29a) blessing, yea, even my blessing, and it shall rest upon him.

30 And now, Zoram, I speak unto you: Behold, thou art the [aservant](#note30a) of Laban; nevertheless, thou hast been brought out of the land of Jerusalem, and I know that thou art a true [bfriend](#note30b) unto my son, Nephi, forever.

31 Wherefore, because thou hast been faithful thy seed shall be blessed [awith](#note31a) his seed, that they dwell in prosperity long upon the face of this land; and nothing, save it shall be iniquity among them, shall harm or disturb their prosperity upon the face of this land forever.

32 Wherefore, if ye shall keep the commandments of the Lord, the Lord hath consecrated this land for the security of thy seed with the seed of my son.

Chapter 2

Redemption comes through the Holy Messiah—Freedom of choice (agency) is essential to existence and progression—Adam fell that men might be—Men are free to choose liberty and eternal life. About 588–570 B.C.

1 And now, Jacob, I speak unto you: Thou art my [afirstborn](#note1a) in the days of my tribulation in the wilderness. And behold, in thy childhood thou hast suffered afflictions and much sorrow, because of the rudeness of thy brethren.

2 Nevertheless, Jacob, my firstborn in the wilderness, thou knowest the greatness of God; and he shall consecrate thine [aafflictions](#note2a) for thy gain.

3 Wherefore, thy soul shall be blessed, and thou shalt dwell safely with thy brother, Nephi; and thy days shall be [aspent](#note3a) in the service of thy God. Wherefore, I know that thou art redeemed, because of the righteousness of thy Redeemer; for thou hast [bbeheld](#note3b) that in the [cfulness](#note3c) of time he cometh to bring salvation unto men.

4 And thou hast [abeheld](#note4a) in thy youth his glory; wherefore, thou art blessed even as they unto whom he shall minister in the flesh; for the Spirit is the same, yesterday, today, and forever. And the way is prepared from the fall of man, and [bsalvation](#note4b) is [cfree](#note4c).

5 And men are instructed sufficiently that they [aknow](#note5a) good from evil. And the [blaw](#note5b) is given unto men. And by the law no flesh is [cjustified](#note5c); or, by the law men are [dcut off](#note5d). Yea, by the temporal law they were cut off; and also, by the spiritual law they perish from that which is good, and become miserable forever.

6 Wherefore, [aredemption](#note6a) cometh in and through the [bHoly](#note6b) [cMessiah](#note6c); for he is full of [dgrace](#note6d) and truth.

7 Behold, he offereth himself a [asacrifice](#note7a) for sin, to answer the ends of the law, unto all those who have a broken heart and a contrite spirit; and unto [bnone](#note7b) else can the [cends](#note7c) of the law be answered.

8 Wherefore, how great the importance to make these things known unto the inhabitants of the earth, that they may know that there is no flesh that can dwell in the presence of God, [asave](#note8a) it be through the merits, and mercy, and grace of the Holy Messiah, who [blayeth](#note8b) down his life according to the flesh, and taketh it again by the power of the Spirit, that he may bring to pass the [cresurrection](#note8c) of the dead, being the first that should rise.

9 Wherefore, he is the firstfruits unto God, inasmuch as he shall make [aintercession](#note9a) for all the children of men; and they that believe in him shall be saved.

10 And because of the intercession for [aall](#note10a), all men come unto God; wherefore, they stand in the presence of him, to be [bjudged](#note10b) of him according to the truth and [choliness](#note10c) which is in him. Wherefore, the ends of the law which the Holy One hath given, unto the inflicting of the [dpunishment](#note10d) which is affixed, which punishment that is affixed is in opposition to that of the happiness which is affixed, to answer the ends of the [eatonement](#note10e)—

11 For it must needs be, that there is an [aopposition](#note11a) in all things. If not so, my firstborn in the wilderness, righteousness could not be brought to pass, neither wickedness, neither holiness nor misery, neither good nor bad. Wherefore, all things must needs be a compound in one; wherefore, if it should be one body it must needs remain as dead, having no life neither death, nor corruption nor incorruption, happiness nor misery, neither sense nor insensibility.

12 Wherefore, it must needs have been created for a thing of naught; wherefore there would have been no [apurpose](#note12a) in the end of its creation. Wherefore, this thing must needs destroy the wisdom of God and his eternal purposes, and also the power, and the mercy, and the [bjustice](#note12b) of God.

13 And if ye shall say there is [ano law](#note13a), ye shall also say there is no sin. If ye shall say there is no sin, ye shall also say there is no righteousness. And if there be no righteousness there be no happiness. And if there be no righteousness nor happiness there be no punishment nor misery. And if these things are not [bthere](#note13b) is no God. And if there is no God we are not, neither the earth; for there could have been no creation of things, neither to act nor to be acted upon; wherefore, all things must have vanished away.

14 And now, my sons, I speak unto you these things for your profit and [alearning](#note14a); for there is a God, and he hath [bcreated](#note14b) all things, both the heavens and the earth, and all things that in them are, both things to act and things to be [cacted](#note14c) upon.

15 And to bring about his eternal [apurposes](#note15a) in the end of man, after he had [bcreated](#note15b) our first parents, and the beasts of the field and the [cfowls](#note15c) of the air, and in fine, all things which are created, it must needs be that there was an opposition; even the [dforbidden](#note15d) [efruit](#note15e) in [fopposition](#note15f) to the [gtree of life](#note15g); the one being sweet and the other bitter.

16 Wherefore, the Lord God gave unto man that he should [aact](#note16a) for himself. Wherefore, man could not [bact](#note16b) for himself save it should be that he was [centiced](#note16c) by the one or the other.

17 And I, Lehi, according to the things which I have read, must needs suppose that an [aangel](#note17a) of God, according to that which is written, had [bfallen](#note17b) from heaven; wherefore, he became a [cdevil](#note17c), having sought that which was evil before God.

18 And because he had fallen from heaven, and had become miserable forever, he [asought](#note18a) also the misery of all mankind. Wherefore, he said unto Eve, yea, even that old serpent, who is the devil, who is the father of all [blies](#note18b), wherefore he said: Partake of the forbidden fruit, and ye shall not die, but ye shall be as God, [cknowing](#note18c) good and evil.

19 And after Adam and Eve had [apartaken](#note19a) of the forbidden fruit they were driven out of the garden of [bEden](#note19b), to till the earth.

20 And they have brought forth children; yea, even the [afamily](#note20a) of all the earth.

21 And the days of the children of [amen](#note21a) were prolonged, according to the [bwill](#note21b) of God, that they might [crepent](#note21c) while in the flesh; wherefore, their state became a state of [dprobation](#note21d), and their time was lengthened, according to the commandments which the Lord God gave unto the children of men. For he gave commandment that all men must repent; for he showed unto all men that they were [elost](#note21e), because of the transgression of their parents.

22 And now, behold, if Adam had not transgressed he would not have fallen, but he would have remained in the garden of Eden. And all things which were created must have remained in the same state in which they were after they were created; and they must have remained forever, and had no end.

23 And they would have had no [achildren](#note23a); wherefore they would have remained in a state of innocence, having no [bjoy](#note23b), for they knew no misery; doing no good, for they knew no [csin](#note23c).

24 But behold, all things have been done in the wisdom of him who [aknoweth](#note24a) all things.

25 [aAdam](#note25a) [bfell](#note25b) that men might be; and men [care](#note25c), that they might have [djoy](#note25d).

26 And the [aMessiah](#note26a) cometh in the fulness of time, that he may [bredeem](#note26b) the children of men from the fall. And because that they are [credeemed](#note26c) from the fall they have become [dfree](#note26d) forever, knowing good from evil; to act for themselves and not to be acted upon, save it be by the punishment of the [elaw](#note26e) at the great and last day, according to the commandments which God hath given.

27 Wherefore, men are [afree](#note27a) according to the [bflesh](#note27b); and [call](#note27c) things are [dgiven](#note27d) them which are expedient unto man. And they are free to [echoose](#note27e) [fliberty](#note27f) and eternal [glife](#note27g), through the great Mediator of all men, or to choose captivity and death, according to the captivity and power of the devil; for he seeketh that all men might be [hmiserable](#note27h) like unto himself.

28 And now, my sons, I would that ye should look to the great [aMediator](#note28a), and hearken unto his great commandments; and be faithful unto his words, and choose eternal life, according to the will of his Holy Spirit;

29 And not choose eternal death, according to the will of the flesh and the [aevil](#note29a) which is therein, which giveth the spirit of the devil power to [bcaptivate](#note29b), to bring you down to [chell](#note29c), that he may reign over you in his own kingdom.

30 I have spoken these few words unto you all, my sons, in the last days of my probation; and I have chosen the good part, according to the words of the prophet. And I have none other object save it be the everlasting [awelfare](#note30a) of your souls. Amen.

Chapter 3

Joseph in Egypt saw the Nephites in vision—He prophesied of Joseph Smith, the latter-day seer; of Moses, who would deliver Israel; and of the coming forth of the Book of Mormon. About 588–570 B.C.

1 And now I speak unto you, Joseph, my [alast-born](#note1a). Thou wast born in the wilderness of mine afflictions; yea, in the days of my greatest sorrow did thy mother bear thee.

2 And may the Lord consecrate also unto thee this [aland](#note2a), which is a most precious land, for thine inheritance and the inheritance of thy seed with thy brethren, for thy security forever, if it so be that ye shall keep the commandments of the Holy One of Israel.

3 And now, Joseph, my last-born, whom I have brought out of the wilderness of mine afflictions, may the Lord bless thee forever, for thy [aseed](#note3a) shall not utterly be [bdestroyed](#note3b).

4 For behold, thou art the fruit of my loins; and I am a descendant of [aJoseph](#note4a) who was carried [bcaptive](#note4b) into Egypt. And great were the [ccovenants](#note4c) of the Lord which he made unto Joseph.

5 Wherefore, Joseph truly [asaw](#note5a) our day. And he obtained a [bpromise](#note5b) of the Lord, that out of the fruit of his loins the Lord God would raise up a [crighteous](#note5c) [dbranch](#note5d) unto the house of Israel; not the Messiah, but a branch which was to be broken off, nevertheless, to be remembered in the covenants of the Lord that the Messiah should be made [emanifest](#note5e) unto them in the latter days, in the spirit of power, unto the bringing of them out of [fdarkness](#note5f) unto light—yea, out of hidden darkness and out of captivity unto freedom.

6 For Joseph truly testified, saying: A [aseer](#note6a) shall the Lord my God raise up, who shall be a choice seer unto the fruit of my [bloins](#note6b).

7 Yea, Joseph truly said: Thus saith the Lord unto me: A choice [aseer](#note7a) will I [braise up](#note7b) out of the fruit of thy loins; and he shall be esteemed highly among the fruit of thy loins. And unto him will I give commandment that he shall do a work for the fruit of thy loins, his brethren, which shall be of great worth unto them, even to the bringing of them to the [cknowledge](#note7c) of the covenants which I have made with thy fathers.

8 And I will give unto him a commandment that he shall do [anone](#note8a) other work, save the work which I shall command him. And I will make him great in mine eyes; for he shall do my work.

9 And he shall be great like unto [aMoses](#note9a), whom I have said I would raise up unto you, to [bdeliver](#note9b) my [cpeople](#note9c), O house of Israel.

10 And [aMoses](#note10a) will I raise up, to deliver thy people out of the land of Egypt.

11 But a [aseer](#note11a) will I raise up out of the fruit of thy loins; and unto him will I give [bpower](#note11b) to [cbring forth](#note11c) my word unto the seed of thy loins—and not to the bringing forth my word only, saith the Lord, but to the convincing them of my word, which shall have already gone forth among them.

12 Wherefore, the fruit of thy loins shall [awrite](#note12a); and the fruit of the loins of [bJudah](#note12b) shall [cwrite](#note12c); and that which shall be written by the fruit of thy loins, and also that which shall be written by the fruit of the loins of Judah, shall grow together, unto the [dconfounding](#note12d) of [efalse doctrines](#note12e) and laying down of contentions, and establishing [fpeace](#note12f) among the fruit of thy loins, and [gbringing](#note12g) them to the [hknowledge](#note12h) of their fathers in the latter days, and also to the knowledge of my covenants, saith the Lord.

13 And out of weakness he shall be made strong, in that day when my work shall commence among all my people, unto the restoring thee, O house of Israel, saith the Lord.

14 And thus prophesied Joseph, saying: Behold, that seer will the Lord bless; and they that seek to destroy him shall be confounded; for this promise, which I have obtained of the Lord, of the fruit of my loins, shall be fulfilled. Behold, I am sure of the fulfilling of this promise;

15 And his [aname](#note15a) shall be called after me; and it shall be after the [bname](#note15b) of his father. And he shall be [clike](#note15c) unto me; for the thing, which the Lord shall bring forth by his hand, by the power of the Lord shall bring [dmy](#note15d) people unto [esalvation](#note15e).

16 Yea, thus prophesied Joseph: I am sure of this thing, even as I am sure of the promise of Moses; for the Lord hath said unto me, I will [apreserve](#note16a) thy seed forever.

17 And the Lord hath said: I will raise up a Moses; and I will give power unto him in a rod; and I will give judgment unto him in writing. Yet I will not loose his tongue, that he shall speak much, for I will not make him mighty in speaking. But I will [awrite](#note17a) unto him my law, by the finger of mine own hand; and I will make a [bspokesman](#note17b) for him.

18 And the Lord said unto me also: I will raise up unto the fruit of thy loins; and I will make for him a spokesman. And I, behold, I will give unto him that he shall write the writing of the fruit of thy loins, unto the fruit of thy loins; and the spokesman of thy loins shall declare it.

19 And the words which he shall write shall be the words which are expedient in my wisdom should go forth unto the [afruit](#note19a) of thy loins. And it shall be as if the fruit of thy loins had cried unto them [bfrom](#note19b) the dust; for I know their faith.

20 And they shall [acry](#note20a) from the [bdust](#note20b); yea, even repentance unto their brethren, even after many generations have gone by them. And it shall come to pass that their cry shall go, even according to the simpleness of their words.

21 Because of their faith their [awords](#note21a) shall proceed forth out of my mouth unto their brethren who are the fruit of thy loins; and the weakness of their words will I make strong in their faith, unto the remembering of my covenant which I made unto thy fathers.

22 And now, behold, my son Joseph, after this manner did my father of old [aprophesy](#note22a).

23 Wherefore, because of this covenant thou art [ablessed](#note23a); for thy seed shall not be destroyed, for they shall [bhearken](#note23b) unto the words of the book.

24 And there shall rise up [aone](#note24a) mighty among them, who shall do much good, both in word and in deed, being an instrument in the hands of God, with exceeding faith, to work mighty wonders, and do that thing which is great in the sight of God, unto the bringing to pass much [brestoration](#note24b) unto the house of Israel, and unto the seed of thy brethren.

25 And now, blessed art thou, Joseph. Behold, thou art little; wherefore hearken unto the words of thy brother, Nephi, and it shall be done unto thee even according to the words which I have spoken. Remember the words of thy dying father. Amen.

Chapter 4

Lehi counsels and blesses his posterity—He dies and is buried—Nephi glories in the goodness of God—Nephi puts his trust in the Lord forever. About 588–570 B.C.

1 And now, I, Nephi, speak concerning the prophecies of which my father hath spoken, concerning [aJoseph](#note1a), who was carried into Egypt.

2 For behold, he truly prophesied concerning all his seed. And the [aprophecies](#note2a) which he wrote, there are not many greater. And he prophesied concerning us, and our future generations; and they are written upon the [bplates of brass](#note2b).

3 Wherefore, after my father had made an end of speaking concerning the prophecies of Joseph, he called the children of Laman, his sons, and his daughters, and said unto them: Behold, my sons, and my daughters, who are the sons and the daughters of my [afirstborn](#note3a), I would that ye should give ear unto my words.

4 For the Lord God hath said that: [aInasmuch](#note4a) as ye shall keep my commandments ye shall prosper in the land; and inasmuch as ye will not keep my commandments ye shall be cut off from my presence.

5 But behold, my sons and my daughters, I cannot go down to my grave save I should leave a [ablessing](#note5a) upon you; for behold, I know that if ye are [bbrought up](#note5b) in the [cway](#note5c) ye should go ye will not depart from it.

6 Wherefore, if ye are [acursed](#note6a), behold, I leave my blessing upon you, that the [bcursing](#note6b) may be taken from you and be answered upon the [cheads](#note6c) of your parents.

7 Wherefore, because of my blessing the Lord God will [anot](#note7a) suffer that ye shall perish; wherefore, he will be [bmerciful](#note7b) unto you and unto your seed forever.

8 And it came to pass that after my father had made an end of speaking to the sons and daughters of Laman, he caused the sons and daughters of Lemuel to be brought before him.

9 And he spake unto them, saying: Behold, my sons and my daughters, who are the sons and the daughters of my second son; behold I leave unto you the same blessing which I left unto the sons and daughters of Laman; wherefore, thou shalt not utterly be destroyed; but in the end thy seed shall be blessed.

10 And it came to pass that when my father had made an end of speaking unto them, behold, he spake unto the sons of [aIshmael](#note10a), yea, and even all his household.

11 And after he had made an end of speaking unto them, he spake unto Sam, saying: Blessed art thou, and thy [aseed](#note11a); for thou shalt inherit the land like unto thy brother Nephi. And thy seed shall be numbered with his seed; and thou shalt be even like unto thy brother, and thy seed like unto his seed; and thou shalt be blessed in all thy days.

12 And it came to pass after my father, Lehi, had [aspoken](#note12a) unto all his household, according to the feelings of his heart and the Spirit of the Lord which was in him, he waxed [bold](#note12b). And it came to pass that he died, and was buried.

13 And it came to pass that not many days after his death, Laman and Lemuel and the sons of Ishmael were [aangry](#note13a) with me because of the admonitions of the Lord.

14 For I, Nephi, was constrained to speak unto them, according to his word; for I had spoken many things unto them, and also my father, before his death; many of which sayings are written upon mine [aother plates](#note14a); for a more history part are written upon mine other plates.

15 And upon [athese](#note15a) I [bwrite](#note15b) the things of my soul, and many of the scriptures which are engraven upon the plates of brass. For my soul [cdelighteth](#note15c) in the scriptures, and my heart [dpondereth](#note15d) them, and writeth them for the [elearning](#note15e) and the profit of my children.

16 Behold, my [asoul](#note16a) delighteth in the things of the Lord; and my [bheart](#note16b) pondereth continually upon the things which I have seen and heard.

17 Nevertheless, notwithstanding the great [agoodness](#note17a) of the Lord, in showing me his great and marvelous works, my heart exclaimeth: O [bwretched](#note17b) man that I am! Yea, my heart [csorroweth](#note17c) because of my flesh; my soul grieveth because of mine iniquities.

18 I am encompassed about, because of the temptations and the sins which do so easily [abeset](#note18a) me.

19 And when I desire to rejoice, my heart groaneth because of my sins; nevertheless, I know in whom I have [atrusted](#note19a).

20 My God hath been my [asupport](#note20a); he hath led me through mine [bafflictions](#note20b) in the wilderness; and he hath preserved me upon the waters of the great deep.

21 He hath filled me with his [alove](#note21a), even unto the [bconsuming](#note21b) of my flesh.

22 He hath confounded mine [aenemies](#note22a), unto the causing of them to quake before me.

23 Behold, he hath heard my cry by day, and he hath given me [aknowledge](#note23a) by [bvisions](#note23b) in the night-time.

24 And by day have I waxed bold in mighty [aprayer](#note24a) before him; yea, my voice have I sent up on high; and angels came down and ministered unto me.

25 And upon the wings of his Spirit hath my body been [acarried away](#note25a) upon exceedingly high mountains. And mine eyes have beheld great things, yea, even too great for man; therefore I was bidden that I should not write them.

26 O then, if I have seen so great things, if the Lord in his condescension unto the children of men hath [avisited](#note26a) men in so much [bmercy](#note26b), [cwhy](#note26c) should my [dheart](#note26d) weep and my soul linger in the valley of sorrow, and my flesh waste away, and my strength slacken, because of mine afflictions?

27 And why should I [ayield](#note27a) to sin, because of my flesh? Yea, why should I give way to [btemptations](#note27b), that the evil one have place in my heart to destroy my [cpeace](#note27c) and afflict my soul? Why am I [dangry](#note27d) because of mine enemy?

28 Awake, my soul! No longer [adroop](#note28a) in sin. Rejoice, O my heart, and give place no more for the [benemy](#note28b) of my soul.

29 Do not [aanger](#note29a) again because of mine enemies. Do not slacken my strength because of mine afflictions.

30 Rejoice, O my [aheart](#note30a), and cry unto the Lord, and say: O Lord, I will praise thee forever; yea, my soul will rejoice in thee, my God, and the [brock](#note30b) of my salvation.

31 O Lord, wilt thou [aredeem](#note31a) my soul? Wilt thou deliver me out of the hands of mine enemies? Wilt thou make me that I may shake at the appearance of [bsin](#note31b)?

32 May the gates of hell be shut continually before me, because that my [aheart](#note32a) is broken and my spirit is contrite! O Lord, wilt thou not shut the gates of thy righteousness before me, that I may [bwalk](#note32b) in the path of the low valley, that I may be strict in the plain road!

33 O Lord, wilt thou encircle me around in the robe of thy [arighteousness](#note33a)! O Lord, wilt thou make a way for mine escape before mine [benemies](#note33b)! Wilt thou make my path straight before me! Wilt thou not place a stumbling block in my way—but that thou wouldst clear my way before me, and hedge not up my way, but the ways of mine enemy.

34 O Lord, I have [atrusted](#note34a) in thee, and I will [btrust](#note34b) in thee forever. I will not put my [ctrust](#note34c) in the arm of flesh; for I know that cursed is he that putteth his [dtrust](#note34d) in the arm of flesh. Yea, cursed is he that putteth his trust in man or maketh flesh his arm.

35 Yea, I know that God will give [aliberally](#note35a) to him that asketh. Yea, my God will give me, if I [bask](#note35b) [cnot](#note35c) amiss; therefore I will lift up my voice unto thee; yea, I will cry unto thee, my God, the [drock](#note35d) of my [erighteousness](#note35e). Behold, my voice shall forever ascend up unto thee, my rock and mine everlasting God. Amen.

Chapter 5

The Nephites separate themselves from the Lamanites, keep the law of Moses, and build a temple—Because of their unbelief, the Lamanites are cut off from the presence of the Lord, are cursed, and become a scourge unto the Nephites. About 588–559 B.C.

1 Behold, it came to pass that I, Nephi, did cry much unto the Lord my God, because of the [aanger](#note1a) of my brethren.

2 But behold, their [aanger](#note2a) did increase against me, insomuch that they did seek to take away my life.

3 Yea, they did murmur against me, saying: Our younger brother thinks to [arule](#note3a) over us; and we have had much trial because of him; wherefore, now let us slay him, that we may not be afflicted more because of his words. For behold, we will not have him to be our ruler; for it belongs unto us, who are the elder brethren, to [brule](#note3b) over this people.

4 Now I do not write upon these plates all the words which they murmured against me. But it sufficeth me to say, that they did seek to take away my life.

5 And it came to pass that the Lord did [awarn](#note5a) me, that I, [bNephi](#note5b), should depart from them and flee into the wilderness, and all those who would go with me.

6 Wherefore, it came to pass that I, Nephi, did take my family, and also [aZoram](#note6a) and his family, and Sam, mine elder brother and his family, and Jacob and Joseph, my younger brethren, and also my sisters, and all those who would go with me. And all those who would go with me were those who believed in the [bwarnings](#note6b) and the revelations of God; wherefore, they did hearken unto my words.

7 And we did take our tents and whatsoever things were possible for us, and did journey in the wilderness for the space of many days. And after we had journeyed for the space of many days we did pitch our tents.

8 And my people would that we should call the name of the place [aNephi](#note8a); wherefore, we did call it Nephi.

9 And all those who were with me did take upon them to call themselves the [apeople](#note9a) of Nephi.

10 And we did observe to keep the judgments, and the [astatutes](#note10a), and the commandments of the Lord in all things, according to the [blaw](#note10b) of Moses.

11 And the Lord was with us; and we did [aprosper](#note11a) exceedingly; for we did sow seed, and we did reap again in abundance. And we began to raise flocks, and herds, and animals of every kind.

12 And I, Nephi, had also brought the records which were engraven upon the [aplates of brass](#note12a); and also the [bball](#note12b), or [ccompass](#note12c), which was prepared for my father by the hand of the Lord, according to that which is written.

13 And it came to pass that we began to prosper exceedingly, and to multiply in the land.

14 And I, Nephi, did take the [asword](#note14a) of Laban, and after the manner of it did make many [bswords](#note14b), lest by any means the people who were now called Lamanites should come upon us and destroy us; for I knew their [chatred](#note14c) towards me and my children and those who were called my people.

15 And I did teach my people to [abuild](#note15a) buildings, and to [bwork](#note15b) in all [cmanner](#note15c) of wood, and of [diron](#note15d), and of copper, and of [ebrass](#note15e), and of steel, and of [fgold](#note15f), and of silver, and of precious ores, which were in great abundance.

16 And I, Nephi, did [abuild](#note16a) a [btemple](#note16b); and I did construct it after the manner of the temple of [cSolomon](#note16c) save it were not built of so many [dprecious](#note16d) things; for they were not to be found upon the land, wherefore, it could not be built like unto Solomon’s [etemple](#note16e). But the manner of the construction was like unto the temple of [fSolomon](#note16f); and the workmanship thereof was exceedingly fine.

17 And it came to pass that I, Nephi, did cause my people to be [aindustrious](#note17a), and to [blabor](#note17b) with their [chands](#note17c).

18 And it came to pass that they would that I should be their [aking](#note18a). But I, Nephi, was desirous that they should have no king; nevertheless, I did for them according to that which was in my power.

19 And behold, the words of the Lord had been fulfilled unto my brethren, which he spake concerning them, that I should be their [aruler](#note19a) and their teacher. Wherefore, I had been their ruler and their [bteacher](#note19b), according to the commandments of the Lord, until the time they sought to take away my life.

20 Wherefore, the word of the Lord was fulfilled which he spake unto me, saying that: Inasmuch as they will [anot hearken](#note20a) unto thy words they shall be [bcut off](#note20b) from the presence of the Lord. And behold, they were [ccut off](#note20c) from his presence.

21 And he had caused the [acursing](#note21a) to come upon them, yea, even a sore cursing, because of their iniquity. For behold, they had hardened their hearts against him, that they had become like unto a flint; wherefore, as they were white, and exceedingly fair and [bdelightsome](#note21b), that they might not be [centicing](#note21c) unto my people the Lord God did cause a [dskin](#note21d) of [eblackness](#note21e) to come upon them.

22 And thus saith the Lord God: I will cause that they shall be [aloathsome](#note22a) unto thy people, save they shall repent of their iniquities.

23 And cursed shall be the seed of him that [amixeth](#note23a) with their seed; for they shall be cursed even with the same cursing. And the Lord spake it, and it was done.

24 And because of their [acursing](#note24a) which was upon them they did become an [bidle](#note24b) people, full of mischief and subtlety, and did seek in the wilderness for beasts of prey.

25 And the Lord God said unto me: They shall be a scourge unto thy seed, to [astir](#note25a) them up in remembrance of me; and inasmuch as they will not remember me, and hearken unto my words, they shall scourge them even unto destruction.

26 And it came to pass that I, Nephi, did [aconsecrate](#note26a) Jacob and Joseph, that they should be [bpriests](#note26b) and [cteachers](#note26c) over the land of my people.

27 And it came to pass that we lived after the manner of [ahappiness](#note27a).

28 And thirty years had passed away from the time we left Jerusalem.

29 And I, Nephi, had kept the [arecords](#note29a) upon my plates, which I had made, of my people thus far.

30 And it came to pass that the Lord God said unto me: [aMake](#note30a) other plates; and thou shalt engraven many things upon them which are good in my sight, for the profit of thy people.

31 Wherefore, I, Nephi, to be obedient to the commandments of the Lord, went and made [athese plates](#note31a) upon which I have engraven these things.

32 And I engraved that which is pleasing unto God. And if my people are pleased with the things of God they will be pleased with mine engravings which are upon these plates.

33 And if my people desire to know the more particular part of the history of my people they must search mine [aother](#note33a) [bplates](#note33b).

34 And it sufficeth me to say that forty years had passed away, and we had already had wars and contentions with our brethren.

Chapter 6

Jacob recounts Jewish history: The Babylonian captivity and return; the ministry and crucifixion of the Holy One of Israel; the help received from the Gentiles; and the Jews’ latter-day restoration when they believe in the Messiah. About 559–545 B.C.

1 The [awords](#note1a) of Jacob, the brother of Nephi, which he spake unto the people of Nephi:

2 Behold, my beloved brethren, I, Jacob, having been called of God, and ordained after the manner of his holy [aorder](#note2a), and having been consecrated by my brother Nephi, unto whom ye look as a [bking](#note2b) or a protector, and on whom ye depend for safety, behold ye know that I have spoken unto you exceedingly many things.

3 Nevertheless, I speak unto you again; for I am desirous for the [awelfare](#note3a) of your souls. Yea, mine anxiety is great for you; and ye yourselves know that it ever has been. For I have exhorted you with all diligence; and I have taught you the words of my father; and I have spoken unto you concerning all things which are [bwritten](#note3b), from the creation of the world.

4 And now, behold, I would speak unto you concerning things which are, and which are to come; wherefore, I will read you the words of [aIsaiah](#note4a). And they are the words which my brother has desired that I should speak unto you. And I speak unto you for your sakes, that ye may learn and glorify the name of your God.

5 And now, the words which I shall read are they which Isaiah spake concerning all the house of Israel; wherefore, they may be [alikened](#note5a) unto you, for ye are of the house of Israel. And there are many things which have been spoken by Isaiah which may be likened unto you, because ye are of the house of Israel.

6 And now, these are the words: [aThus](#note6a) saith the Lord God: Behold, I will lift up mine hand to the Gentiles, and set up my [bstandard](#note6b) to the people; and they shall bring thy sons in their arms, and thy daughters shall be carried upon their shoulders.

7 And [akings](#note7a) shall be thy nursing fathers, and their queens thy nursing mothers; they shall bow down to thee with their faces towards the earth, and lick up the dust of thy feet; and thou shalt know that [bI am](#note7b) the Lord; for they shall not be ashamed that [cwait](#note7c) for me.

8 And now I, Jacob, would speak somewhat concerning these words. For behold, the Lord has shown me that those who were at [aJerusalem](#note8a), from whence we came, have been [bslain](#note8b) and [ccarried away](#note8c) captive.

9 Nevertheless, the Lord has shown unto me that they should [areturn](#note9a) again. And he also has shown unto me that the Lord God, the Holy One of Israel, should manifest himself unto them in the flesh; and after he should manifest himself they should [bscourge](#note9b) him and [ccrucify](#note9c) him, according to the words of the angel who spake it unto me.

10 And after they have [ahardened](#note10a) their hearts and [bstiffened](#note10b) their necks against the Holy One of Israel, behold, the [cjudgments](#note10c) of the Holy One of Israel shall come upon them. And the day cometh that they shall be smitten and afflicted.

11 Wherefore, after they are driven to and fro, for thus saith the angel, many shall be afflicted in the flesh, and shall not be suffered to [aperish](#note11a), because of the prayers of the faithful; they shall be scattered, and smitten, and hated; nevertheless, the Lord will be merciful unto them, that [bwhen](#note11b) they shall come to the [cknowledge](#note11c) of their Redeemer, they shall be [dgathered](#note11d) together again to the [elands](#note11e) of their inheritance.

12 And blessed are the [aGentiles](#note12a), they of whom the prophet has written; for behold, if it so be that they shall repent and fight not against Zion, and do not unite themselves to that great and [babominable](#note12b) church, they shall be saved; for the Lord God will fulfil his [ccovenants](#note12c) which he has made unto his children; and for this cause the prophet has written these things.

13 Wherefore, they that fight against Zion and the covenant people of the Lord shall lick up the dust of their feet; and the people of the Lord shall not be [aashamed](#note13a). For the people of the Lord are they who [bwait](#note13b) for him; for they still wait for the coming of the Messiah.

14 And behold, according to the words of the prophet, the Messiah will set himself again the [asecond](#note14a) time to recover them; wherefore, he will [bmanifest](#note14b) himself unto them in power and great glory, unto the [cdestruction](#note14c) of their enemies, when that day cometh when they shall believe in him; and none will he destroy that believe in him.

15 And they that believe not in him shall be [adestroyed](#note15a), both by [bfire](#note15b), and by tempest, and by earthquakes, and by [cbloodsheds](#note15c), and by [dpestilence](#note15d), and by [efamine](#note15e). And they shall know that the Lord is God, the Holy One of Israel.

16 [aFor](#note16a) shall the prey be taken from the mighty, or the [blawful captive](#note16b) delivered?

17 But thus saith the Lord: Even the captives of the mighty shall be taken away, and the prey of the terrible shall be delivered; [afor](#note17a) the [bMighty God](#note17b) shall [cdeliver](#note17c) his covenant people. For thus saith the Lord: I will contend with them that contendeth with thee—

18 And I will feed them that oppress thee, with their own flesh; and they shall be drunken with their own blood as with sweet wine; and all flesh shall know that I the Lord am thy Savior and thy [aRedeemer](#note18a), the [bMighty One](#note18b) of Jacob.

Chapter 7

Jacob continues reading from Isaiah: Isaiah speaks messianically—The Messiah will have the tongue of the learned—He will give His back to the smiters—He will not be confounded—Compare Isaiah 50. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aYea](#note1a), for thus saith the Lord: Have I put thee away, or have I cast thee off forever? For thus saith the Lord: Where is the [bbill](#note1b) of your mother’s [cdivorcement](#note1c)? To whom have I put thee away, or to which of my [dcreditors](#note1d) have I [esold](#note1e) you? Yea, to whom have I sold you? Behold, for your iniquities have ye sold yourselves, and for your transgressions is your mother put away.

2 Wherefore, when I came, there was no man; when I [acalled](#note2a), yea, there was none to answer. O house of Israel, is my hand shortened at all that it cannot redeem, or have I no power to deliver? Behold, at my rebuke I [bdry up](#note2b) the [csea](#note2c), I make their [drivers](#note2d) a wilderness and their [efish](#note2e) to stink because the waters are dried up, and they die because of thirst.

3 I clothe the heavens with [ablackness](#note3a), and I make [bsackcloth](#note3b) their covering.

4 The Lord God hath given me the [atongue](#note4a) of the learned, that I should know how to speak a word in season unto thee, O house of Israel. When ye are weary he waketh morning by morning. He waketh mine ear to hear as the learned.

5 The Lord God hath opened mine [aear](#note5a), and I was not rebellious, neither turned away back.

6 I gave my back to the [asmiter](#note6a), and my cheeks to them that plucked off the hair. I hid not my face from [bshame](#note6b) and spitting.

7 For the Lord God will help me, therefore shall I not be confounded. Therefore have I set my face like a flint, and I know that I shall not be [aashamed](#note7a).

8 And the Lord is near, and he [ajustifieth](#note8a) me. Who will contend with me? Let us stand together. Who is mine adversary? Let him come near me, and I will [bsmite](#note8b) him with the strength of my mouth.

9 For the Lord God will help me. And all they who shall [acondemn](#note9a) me, behold, all they shall [bwax old](#note9b) as a garment, and the moth shall eat them up.

10 Who is among you that feareth the Lord, that obeyeth the [avoice](#note10a) of his servant, that [bwalketh](#note10b) in darkness and hath no light?

11 Behold all ye that kindle fire, that compass yourselves about with sparks, walk in the light of [ayour](#note11a) fire and in the sparks which ye have kindled. [bThis](#note11b) shall ye have of mine hand—ye shall lie down in sorrow.

Chapter 8

Jacob continues reading from Isaiah: In the last days, the Lord will comfort Zion and gather Israel—The redeemed will come to Zion amid great joy—Compare Isaiah 51 and 52:1–2. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aHearken](#note1a) unto me, ye that follow after righteousness. Look unto the [brock](#note1b) from whence ye are hewn, and to the hole of the pit from whence ye are digged.

2 Look unto Abraham, your [afather](#note2a), and unto [bSarah](#note2b), she that bare you; for I called him alone, and blessed him.

3 For the Lord shall [acomfort](#note3a) [bZion](#note3b), he will comfort all her waste places; and he will make her [cwilderness](#note3c) like [dEden](#note3d), and her desert like the garden of the Lord. Joy and gladness shall be found therein, thanksgiving and the voice of melody.

4 Hearken unto me, my people; and give ear unto me, O my nation; for a [alaw](#note4a) shall proceed from me, and I will make my judgment to rest for a [blight](#note4b) for the people.

5 My righteousness is near; my [asalvation](#note5a) is gone forth, and mine arm shall [bjudge](#note5b) the people. The [cisles](#note5c) shall wait upon me, and on mine arm shall they trust.

6 Lift up your eyes to the [aheavens](#note6a), and look upon the earth beneath; for the heavens shall [bvanish](#note6b) away like smoke, and the earth shall [cwax old](#note6c) like a garment; and they that dwell therein shall die in like manner. But my salvation shall be forever, and my righteousness shall not be abolished.

7 Hearken unto me, ye that know righteousness, the people in whose heart I have written my law, [afear](#note7a) ye not the [breproach](#note7b) of men, neither be ye afraid of their [crevilings](#note7c).

8 For the [amoth](#note8a) shall eat them up like a garment, and the worm shall eat them like wool. But my righteousness shall be forever, and my salvation from generation to generation.

9 [aAwake](#note9a), awake! Put on [bstrength](#note9b), O arm of the Lord; awake as in the ancient days. Art thou not he that hath cut [cRahab](#note9c), and wounded the [ddragon](#note9d)?

10 Art thou not he who hath dried the sea, the waters of the great deep; that hath made the depths of the sea a [away](#note10a) for the ransomed to pass over?

11 Therefore, the [aredeemed](#note11a) of the Lord shall [breturn](#note11b), and come with [csinging](#note11c) unto Zion; and everlasting joy and holiness shall be upon their heads; and they shall obtain gladness and joy; sorrow and [dmourning](#note11d) shall flee away.

12 [aI](#note12a) am he; yea, I am he that comforteth you. Behold, who art thou, that thou shouldst be [bafraid](#note12b) of man, who shall die, and of the son of man, who shall be made like unto [cgrass](#note12c)?

13 And [aforgettest](#note13a) the Lord thy maker, that hath [bstretched](#note13b) forth the heavens, and laid the foundations of the earth, and hast feared continually every day, because of the fury of the [coppressor](#note13c), as if he were ready to destroy? And where is the fury of the oppressor?

14 The [acaptive](#note14a) exile hasteneth, that he may be loosed, and that he should not die in the pit, nor that his bread should fail.

15 But I am the Lord thy God, whose [awaves](#note15a) roared; the Lord of Hosts is my name.

16 And I have [aput](#note16a) my words in thy mouth, and have covered thee in the shadow of mine hand, that I may plant the heavens and lay the foundations of the earth, and say unto Zion: Behold, thou art my [bpeople](#note16b).

17 Awake, awake, stand up, O Jerusalem, which hast drunk at the hand of the Lord the [acup](#note17a) of his [bfury](#note17b)—thou hast drunken the dregs of the cup of trembling wrung out—

18 And none to guide her among all the sons she hath brought forth; neither that taketh her by the hand, of all the sons she hath brought up.

19 These two [asons](#note19a) are come unto thee, who shall be sorry for thee—thy desolation and destruction, and the famine and the sword—and by whom shall I comfort thee?

20 Thy sons have fainted, save these two; they lie at the head of all the streets; as a wild bull in a net, they are full of the fury of the Lord, the rebuke of thy God.

21 Therefore hear now this, thou afflicted, and [adrunken](#note21a), and not with wine:

22 Thus saith thy Lord, the Lord and thy God [apleadeth](#note22a) the cause of his people; behold, I have taken out of thine hand the cup of trembling, the dregs of the cup of my fury; thou shalt no more drink it again.

23 But [aI](#note23a) will put it into the hand of them that afflict thee; who have said to thy soul: Bow down, that we may go over—and thou hast laid thy body as the ground and as the street to them that went over.

24 [aAwake](#note24a), awake, put on thy [bstrength](#note24b), O [cZion](#note24c); put on thy beautiful garments, O Jerusalem, the holy city; for henceforth there shall [dno more](#note24d) come into thee the uncircumcised and the unclean.

25 Shake thyself from the dust; arise, sit down, O Jerusalem; loose thyself from the [abands](#note25a) of thy neck, O captive daughter of Zion.

Chapter 9

Jacob explains that the Jews will be gathered in all their lands of promise—The Atonement ransoms man from the Fall—The bodies of the dead will come forth from the grave, and their spirits from hell and from paradise—They will be judged—The Atonement saves from death, hell, the devil, and endless torment—The righteous are to be saved in the kingdom of God—Penalties for sins are set forth—The Holy One of Israel is the keeper of the gate. About 559–545 B.C.

1 And now, my beloved brethren, I have read these things that ye might know concerning the [acovenants](#note1a) of the Lord that he has covenanted with all the house of Israel—

2 That he has spoken unto the Jews, by the mouth of his holy prophets, even from the beginning down, from generation to generation, until the time comes that they shall be [arestored](#note2a) to the true church and fold of God; when they shall be [bgathered](#note2b) home to the [clands](#note2c) of their inheritance, and shall be established in all their lands of promise.

3 Behold, my beloved brethren, I speak unto you these things that ye may rejoice, and [alift up](#note3a) your heads forever, because of the blessings which the Lord God shall bestow upon your children.

4 For I know that ye have searched much, many of you, to know of things to come; wherefore I know that ye know that our [aflesh](#note4a) must waste away and die; nevertheless, in our [bbodies](#note4b) we shall see God.

5 Yea, I know that ye know that in the body he shall show himself unto those at Jerusalem, from whence we came; for it is expedient that it should be among them; for it behooveth the great [aCreator](#note5a) that he [bsuffereth](#note5b) himself to become [csubject](#note5c) unto man in the flesh, and [ddie](#note5d) for [eall](#note5e) men, that all men might become subject unto him.

6 For as [adeath](#note6a) hath passed upon all men, to fulfil the merciful [bplan](#note6b) of the great Creator, there must needs be a power of [cresurrection](#note6c), and the resurrection must needs come unto man by reason of the [dfall](#note6d); and the fall came by reason of [etransgression](#note6e); and because man became fallen they were [fcut off](#note6f) from the [gpresence](#note6g) of the Lord.

7 Wherefore, it must needs be an [ainfinite](#note7a) [batonement](#note7b)—save it should be an infinite atonement this corruption could not put on incorruption. Wherefore, the [cfirst](#note7c) judgment which came upon man must needs have [dremained](#note7d) to an endless duration. And if so, this flesh must have laid down to rot and to crumble to its mother earth, to rise no more.

8 O the [awisdom](#note8a) of God, his [bmercy](#note8b) and [cgrace](#note8c)! For behold, if the [dflesh](#note8d) should rise no more our spirits must become subject to that angel who [efell](#note8e) from before the presence of the Eternal God, and became the [fdevil](#note8f), to rise no more.

9 And our spirits must have become [alike](#note9a) unto him, and we become devils, [bangels](#note9b) to a [cdevil](#note9c), to be [dshut out](#note9d) from the presence of our God, and to remain with the father of [elies](#note9e), in misery, like unto himself; yea, to that being who [fbeguiled](#note9f) our first parents, who [gtransformeth](#note9g) himself nigh unto an [hangel](#note9h) of light, and [istirreth up](#note9i) the children of men unto [jsecret combinations](#note9j) of murder and all manner of secret works of darkness.

10 O how great the [agoodness](#note10a) of our God, who prepareth a way for our [bescape](#note10b) from the grasp of this awful monster; yea, that monster, [cdeath](#note10c) and [dhell](#note10d), which I call the death of the body, and also the death of the spirit.

11 And because of the way of [adeliverance](#note11a) of our God, the Holy One of Israel, this [bdeath](#note11b), of which I have spoken, which is the temporal, shall deliver up its dead; which death is the grave.

12 And this [adeath](#note12a) of which I have spoken, which is the spiritual death, shall deliver up its dead; which spiritual death is [bhell](#note12b); wherefore, death and hell must [cdeliver](#note12c) up their dead, and hell must deliver up its [dcaptive](#note12d) [espirits](#note12e), and the grave must deliver up its captive [fbodies](#note12f), and the bodies and the [gspirits](#note12g) of men will be [hrestored](#note12h) one to the other; and it is by the power of the resurrection of the Holy One of Israel.

13 O how great the [aplan](#note13a) of our God! For on the other hand, the [bparadise](#note13b) of God must deliver up the spirits of the righteous, and the grave deliver up the body of the righteous; and the spirit and the body is [crestored](#note13c) to itself again, and all men become incorruptible, and [dimmortal](#note13d), and they are living souls, having a [eperfect](#note13e) [fknowledge](#note13f) like unto us in the flesh, save it be that our knowledge shall be perfect.

14 Wherefore, we shall have a [aperfect](#note14a) [bknowledge](#note14b) of all our [cguilt](#note14c), and our [duncleanness](#note14d), and our [enakedness](#note14e); and the righteous shall have a perfect knowledge of their enjoyment, and their [frighteousness](#note14f), being [gclothed](#note14g) with [hpurity](#note14h), yea, even with the [irobe](#note14i) of righteousness.

15 And it shall come to pass that when all men shall have passed from this first death unto life, insomuch as they have become immortal, they must appear before the [ajudgment-seat](#note15a) of the Holy One of Israel; and then cometh the [bjudgment](#note15b), and then must they be judged according to the holy judgment of God.

16 And assuredly, as the Lord liveth, for the Lord God hath spoken it, and it is his eternal [aword](#note16a), which cannot [bpass away](#note16b), that they who are righteous shall be righteous still, and they who are [cfilthy](#note16c) shall be [dfilthy](#note16d) still; wherefore, they who are filthy are the [edevil](#note16e) and his angels; and they shall go away into [feverlasting](#note16f) fire, prepared for them; and their [gtorment](#note16g) is as a [hlake](#note16h) of fire and brimstone, whose flame ascendeth up forever and ever and has no end.

17 O the greatness and the [ajustice](#note17a) of our God! For he executeth all his words, and they have gone forth out of his mouth, and his law must be [bfulfilled](#note17b).

18 But, behold, the [arighteous](#note18a), the [bsaints](#note18b) of the Holy One of Israel, they who have believed in the Holy One of Israel, they who have endured the [ccrosses](#note18c) of the world, and despised the shame of it, they shall [dinherit](#note18d) the [ekingdom](#note18e) of God, which was prepared for them [ffrom](#note18f) the foundation of the world, and their [gjoy](#note18g) shall be full [hforever](#note18h).

19 O the greatness of the mercy of our God, the Holy One of Israel! For he [adelivereth](#note19a) his saints from that [bawful](#note19b) monster the devil, and death, and [chell](#note19c), and that lake of fire and brimstone, which is endless torment.

20 O how great the [aholiness](#note20a) of our God! For he [bknoweth](#note20b) [call](#note20c) things, and there is not anything save he knows it.

21 And he cometh into the world that he may [asave](#note21a) all men if they will hearken unto his voice; for behold, he suffereth the pains of all men, yea, the [bpains](#note21b) of every living creature, both men, women, and children, who belong to the family of [cAdam](#note21c).

22 And he suffereth this that the resurrection might pass upon all men, that all might stand before him at the great and judgment day.

23 And he commandeth all men that they must [arepent](#note23a), and be [bbaptized](#note23b) in his name, having perfect [cfaith](#note23c) in the Holy One of Israel, or they cannot be saved in the kingdom of God.

24 And if they will not repent and believe in his [aname](#note24a), and be baptized in his name, and [bendure](#note24b) to the end, they must be [cdamned](#note24c); for the Lord God, the Holy One of Israel, has spoken it.

25 Wherefore, he has given a [alaw](#note25a); and where there is [bno](#note25b) [claw](#note25c) given there is no [dpunishment](#note25d); and where there is no punishment there is no condemnation; and where there is no condemnation the mercies of the Holy One of Israel have claim upon them, because of the atonement; for they are delivered by the power of him.

26 For the [aatonement](#note26a) satisfieth the demands of his [bjustice](#note26b) upon all those who [chave](#note26c) not the [dlaw](#note26d) given to them, that they are [edelivered](#note26e) from that awful monster, death and [fhell](#note26f), and the devil, and the lake of fire and brimstone, which is endless torment; and they are restored to that God who gave them [gbreath](#note26g), which is the Holy One of Israel.

27 But wo unto him that has the [alaw](#note27a) given, yea, that has all the commandments of God, like unto us, and that [btransgresseth](#note27b) them, and that [cwasteth](#note27c) the days of his [dprobation](#note27d), for awful is his state!

28 O that cunning [aplan](#note28a) of the evil one! O the [bvainness](#note28b), and the frailties, and the [cfoolishness](#note28c) of men! When they are [dlearned](#note28d) they think they are [ewise](#note28e), and they [fhearken not](#note28f) unto the [gcounsel](#note28g) of God, for they set it aside, supposing they know of themselves, wherefore, their [hwisdom](#note28h) is foolishness and it profiteth them not. And they shall perish.

29 But to be [alearned](#note29a) is good if they [bhearken](#note29b) unto the [ccounsels](#note29c) of God.

30 But wo unto the [arich](#note30a), who are [brich](#note30b) as to the things of the [cworld](#note30c). For because they are rich they despise the [dpoor](#note30d), and they persecute the meek, and their [ehearts](#note30e) are upon their treasures; wherefore, their [ftreasure](#note30f) is their god. And behold, their [gtreasure](#note30g) shall perish with them also.

31 And wo unto the deaf that will not [ahear](#note31a); for they shall perish.

32 Wo unto the [ablind](#note32a) that will not see; for they shall perish also.

33 Wo unto the [auncircumcised](#note33a) of heart, for a knowledge of their iniquities shall smite them at the last day.

34 Wo unto the [aliar](#note34a), for he shall be thrust down to [bhell](#note34b).

35 Wo unto the [amurderer](#note35a) who deliberately [bkilleth](#note35b), for he shall [cdie](#note35c).

36 Wo unto them who commit [awhoredoms](#note36a), for they shall be thrust down to hell.

37 Yea, wo unto those that [aworship](#note37a) idols, for the devil of all devils delighteth in them.

38 And, in fine, wo unto all those who die in their [asins](#note38a); for they shall [breturn](#note38b) to God, and behold his face, and remain in their sins.

39 O, my beloved brethren, remember the awfulness in [atransgressing](#note39a) against that Holy God, and also the awfulness of yielding to the enticings of that [bcunning](#note39b) one. Remember, to be [ccarnally-minded](#note39c) is [ddeath](#note39d), and to be [espiritually-minded](#note39e) is [flife](#note39f) [geternal](#note39g).

40 O, my beloved brethren, give ear to my words. Remember the greatness of the Holy One of Israel. Do not say that I have spoken hard things against you; for if ye do, ye will [arevile](#note40a) against the [btruth](#note40b); for I have spoken the words of your Maker. I know that the words of truth are [chard](#note40c) against all [duncleanness](#note40d); but the [erighteous](#note40e) fear them not, for they love the truth and are not shaken.

41 O then, my beloved brethren, [acome](#note41a) unto the Lord, the Holy One. Remember that his paths are righteous. Behold, the [bway](#note41b) for man is [cnarrow](#note41c), but it lieth in a straight course before him, and the keeper of the [dgate](#note41d) is the Holy One of Israel; and he employeth no servant there; and there is none other way save it be by the gate; for he cannot be deceived, for the Lord God is his name.

42 And whoso [aknocketh](#note42a), to him will he open; and the [bwise](#note42b), and the learned, and they that are rich, who are puffed up because of their [clearning](#note42c), and their [dwisdom](#note42d), and their riches—yea, they are they whom he despiseth; and save they shall cast these things away, and consider themselves [efools](#note42e) before God, and come down in the depths of [fhumility](#note42f), he will not open unto them.

43 But the things of the wise and the [aprudent](#note43a) shall be [bhid](#note43b) from them forever—yea, that happiness which is prepared for the saints.

44 O, my beloved brethren, remember my words. Behold, I take off my garments, and I shake them before you; I pray the God of my salvation that he view me with his [aall-searching](#note44a) eye; wherefore, ye shall know at the last day, when all men shall be judged of their works, that the God of Israel did witness that I [bshook](#note44b) your iniquities from my soul, and that I stand with brightness before him, and am [crid](#note44c) of your blood.

45 O, my beloved brethren, turn away from your sins; shake off the [achains](#note45a) of him that would bind you fast; come unto that God who is the [brock](#note45b) of your salvation.

46 Prepare your souls for that glorious day when [ajustice](#note46a) shall be administered unto the righteous, even the day of [bjudgment](#note46b), that ye may not shrink with awful fear; that ye may not remember your awful [cguilt](#note46c) in perfectness, and be constrained to exclaim: Holy, holy are thy judgments, O Lord God [dAlmighty](#note46d)—but I know my guilt; I transgressed thy law, and my transgressions are mine; and the devil hath [eobtained](#note46e) me, that I am a prey to his awful misery.

47 But behold, my brethren, is it expedient that I should awake you to an awful reality of these things? Would I harrow up your souls if your minds were pure? Would I be plain unto you according to the plainness of the truth if ye were freed from sin?

48 Behold, if ye were holy I would speak unto you of holiness; but as ye are not holy, and ye look upon me as a [ateacher](#note48a), it must needs be expedient that I [bteach](#note48b) you the consequences of sin.

49 Behold, my soul abhorreth sin, and my heart [adelighteth](#note49a) in righteousness; and I will [bpraise](#note49b) the holy name of my God.

50 Come, my brethren, every one that [athirsteth](#note50a), come ye to the [bwaters](#note50b); and he that hath no [cmoney](#note50c), come buy and eat; yea, come buy wine and milk without money and without price.

51 Wherefore, do not spend money for that which is of no worth, nor your [alabor](#note51a) for that which cannot [bsatisfy](#note51b). Hearken diligently unto me, and remember the words which I have spoken; and come unto the Holy One of Israel, and [cfeast](#note51c) upon that which perisheth not, neither can be corrupted, and let your soul delight in fatness.

52 Behold, my beloved brethren, remember the words of your God; pray unto him continually by day, and give [athanks](#note52a) unto his holy name by night. Let your hearts [brejoice](#note52b).

53 And behold how great the [acovenants](#note53a) of the Lord, and how great his [bcondescensions](#note53b) unto the children of men; and because of his greatness, and his [cgrace](#note53c) and [dmercy](#note53d), he has promised unto us that our seed shall not utterly be destroyed, according to the flesh, but that he would [epreserve](#note53e) them; and in future generations they shall become a righteous [fbranch](#note53f) unto the house of Israel.

54 And now, my brethren, I would speak unto you more; but on the morrow I will declare unto you the remainder of my words. Amen.

Chapter 10

Jacob explains that the Jews will crucify their God—They will be scattered until they begin to believe in Him—America will be a land of liberty where no king will rule—Reconcile yourselves to God and gain salvation through His grace. About 559–545 B.C.

1 And now I, Jacob, speak unto you again, my beloved brethren, concerning this righteous [abranch](#note1a) of which I have spoken.

2 For behold, the [apromises](#note2a) which we have obtained are promises unto us according to the flesh; wherefore, as it has been shown unto me that many of our children shall perish in the flesh because of [bunbelief](#note2b), nevertheless, God will be merciful unto many; and our children shall be [crestored](#note2c), that they may come to that which will give them the true knowledge of their Redeemer.

3 Wherefore, as I said unto you, it must needs be expedient that Christ—for in the last night the [aangel](#note3a) spake unto me that this should be his name—should [bcome](#note3b) among the [cJews](#note3c), among those who are the more wicked part of the world; and they shall [dcrucify](#note3d) him—for thus it behooveth our God, and there is none other nation on earth that would [ecrucify](#note3e) their [fGod](#note3f).

4 For should the mighty [amiracles](#note4a) be wrought among other nations they would repent, and know that he be their God.

5 But because of [apriestcrafts](#note5a) and iniquities, they at Jerusalem will [bstiffen](#note5b) their necks against him, that he be [ccrucified](#note5c).

6 Wherefore, because of their iniquities, destructions, famines, [apestilences](#note6a), and bloodshed shall come upon them; and they who shall not be destroyed shall be [bscattered](#note6b) among all nations.

7 But behold, thus saith the [aLord God](#note7a): [bWhen](#note7b) the day cometh that they shall believe in me, that I am Christ, then have I covenanted with their fathers that they shall be [crestored](#note7c) in the flesh, upon the earth, unto the [dlands](#note7d) of their inheritance.

8 And it shall come to pass that they shall be [agathered](#note8a) in from their long dispersion, from the [bisles](#note8b) of the sea, and from the four parts of the earth; and the nations of the Gentiles shall be great in the eyes of me, saith God, in [ccarrying](#note8c) them forth to the lands of their inheritance.

9 [aYea](#note9a), the kings of the Gentiles shall be nursing fathers unto them, and their queens shall become nursing mothers; wherefore, the [bpromises](#note9b) of the Lord are great unto the Gentiles, for he hath spoken it, and who can dispute?

10 But behold, this land, said God, shall be a land of thine inheritance, and the [aGentiles](#note10a) shall be blessed upon the land.

11 And this land shall be a land of [aliberty](#note11a) unto the Gentiles, and there shall be no [bkings](#note11b) upon the land, who shall raise up unto the Gentiles.

12 And I will fortify this land [aagainst](#note12a) all other nations.

13 And he that [afighteth](#note13a) against Zion shall [bperish](#note13b), saith God.

14 For he that raiseth up a [aking](#note14a) against me shall perish, for I, the Lord, the [bking](#note14b) of heaven, will be their king, and I will be a [clight](#note14c) unto them forever, that hear my words.

15 Wherefore, for this cause, that my [acovenants](#note15a) may be fulfilled which I have made unto the children of men, that I will do unto them while they are in the flesh, I must needs destroy the [bsecret](#note15b) works of [cdarkness](#note15c), and of murders, and of abominations.

16 Wherefore, he that [afighteth](#note16a) against [bZion](#note16b), both Jew and Gentile, both bond and free, both male and female, [cshall](#note16c) perish; for [dthey](#note16d) are they who are the [ewhore](#note16e) of all the earth; for [fthey](#note16f) who are [gnot](#note16g) for me are [hagainst](#note16h) me, saith our God.

17 For I will [afulfil](#note17a) my [bpromises](#note17b) which I have made unto the children of men, that I will do unto them while they are in the flesh—

18 Wherefore, my beloved brethren, thus saith our God: I will afflict thy seed by the hand of the Gentiles; nevertheless, I will [asoften](#note18a) the hearts of the [bGentiles](#note18b), that they shall be like unto a father to them; wherefore, the Gentiles shall be [cblessed](#note18c) and [dnumbered](#note18d) among the house of Israel.

19 Wherefore, I will [aconsecrate](#note19a) this land unto thy seed, and them who shall be numbered among thy seed, forever, for the land of their inheritance; for it is a choice land, saith God unto me, above all other lands, wherefore I will have all men that dwell thereon that they shall worship me, saith God.

20 And now, my beloved brethren, seeing that our merciful God has given us so great knowledge concerning these things, let us remember him, and lay aside our sins, and not hang down our heads, for we are not cast off; nevertheless, we have been [adriven out](#note20a) of the land of our inheritance; but we have been led to a [bbetter land](#note20b), for the Lord has made the sea our [cpath](#note20c), and we are upon an [disle](#note20d) of the sea.

21 But great are the promises of the Lord unto them who are upon the [aisles](#note21a) of the sea; wherefore as it says isles, there must needs be more than this, and they are inhabited also by our brethren.

22 For behold, the Lord God has [aled away](#note22a) from time to time from the house of Israel, according to his will and pleasure. And now behold, the Lord remembereth all them who have been broken off, wherefore he remembereth us also.

23 Therefore, [acheer up](#note23a) your hearts, and remember that ye are [bfree](#note23b) to [cact](#note23c) for yourselves—to [dchoose](#note23d) the way of everlasting death or the way of eternal life.

24 Wherefore, my beloved brethren, [areconcile](#note24a) yourselves to the [bwill](#note24b) of God, and not to the will of the devil and the flesh; and remember, after ye are reconciled unto God, that it is only in and through the [cgrace](#note24c) of God that ye are [dsaved](#note24d).

25 Wherefore, may God [araise](#note25a) you from death by the power of the resurrection, and also from everlasting death by the power of the [batonement](#note25b), that ye may be received into the [ceternal](#note25c) kingdom of God, that ye may praise him through grace divine. Amen.

Chapter 11

Jacob saw his Redeemer—The law of Moses typifies Christ and proves He will come. About 559–545 B.C.

1 And now, [aJacob](#note1a) spake many more things to my people at that time; nevertheless only these things have I caused to be [bwritten](#note1b), for the things which I have written sufficeth me.

2 And now I, Nephi, write [amore](#note2a) of the words of [bIsaiah](#note2b), for my soul delighteth in his words. For I will liken his words unto my people, and I will send them forth unto all my children, for he verily [csaw](#note2c) my [dRedeemer](#note2d), even as I have seen him.

3 And my brother, Jacob, also has [aseen](#note3a) him as I have seen him; wherefore, I will send their words forth unto my children to prove unto them that my words are true. Wherefore, by the words of [bthree](#note3b), God hath said, I will establish my word. Nevertheless, God sendeth more [cwitnesses](#note3c), and he proveth all his words.

4 Behold, my soul delighteth in [aproving](#note4a) unto my people the truth of the [bcoming](#note4b) of Christ; for, for this end hath the [claw](#note4c) of Moses been given; and all things which have been given of God from the beginning of the world, unto man, are the [dtypifying](#note4d) of him.

5 And also my soul delighteth in the [acovenants](#note5a) of the Lord which he hath made to our fathers; yea, my soul delighteth in his [bgrace](#note5b), and in his justice, and power, and mercy in the great and eternal plan of [cdeliverance](#note5c) from death.

6 And my soul delighteth in proving unto my people that [asave](#note6a) Christ should come all men must perish.

7 For if there be [ano](#note7a) Christ there be no God; and if there be no God we are not, for there could have been no [bcreation](#note7b). But there is a God, and [che](#note7c) is Christ, and he cometh in the fulness of his own time.

8 And now I write [asome](#note8a) of the words of Isaiah, that whoso of my people shall see these words may lift up their hearts and rejoice for all men. Now these are the words, and ye may liken them unto you and unto all men.
