* [◀](#ldsBACK_note8a)

  8a

  See the Latter-day Saint edition of the King James Version of the Bible for other notes and cross-references on these chapters from Isaiah.

Chapter 12

Isaiah sees the latter-day temple, gathering of Israel, and millennial judgment and peace—The proud and wicked will be brought low at the Second Coming—Compare Isaiah 2. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aThe](#note1a) word that Isaiah, the son of Amoz, saw concerning Judah and Jerusalem:

2 And it shall come to pass in the last days, [awhen](#note2a) the [bmountain](#note2b) of the Lord’s [chouse](#note2c) shall be established in the top of the [dmountains](#note2d), and shall be exalted above the hills, and all nations shall flow unto it.

3 And many [apeople](#note3a) shall go and say, Come ye, and let us go up to the [bmountain](#note3b) of the Lord, to the [chouse](#note3c) of the God of Jacob; and he will teach us of his ways, and we will [dwalk](#note3d) in his paths; for out of Zion shall go forth the law, and the word of the Lord from Jerusalem.

4 And he shall [ajudge](#note4a) among the nations, and shall rebuke many people: and they shall beat their swords into plow-shares, and their spears into pruning-hooks—nation shall not lift up sword against nation, neither shall they learn war any more.

5 O house of Jacob, come ye and let us walk in the light of the Lord; yea, come, for ye have all [agone astray](#note5a), every one to his [bwicked](#note5b) ways.

6 Therefore, O Lord, thou hast forsaken thy people, the house of Jacob, because they be replenished from the east, and hearken unto [asoothsayers](#note6a) like the [bPhilistines](#note6b), and they please themselves in the children of strangers.

7 Their land also is full of silver and gold, neither is there any end of their [atreasures](#note7a); their land is also full of horses, neither is there any end of their chariots.

8 Their land is also full of [aidols](#note8a); they worship the work of their own hands, that which their own fingers have made.

9 And the mean man [aboweth](#note9a) [bnot](#note9b) down, and the great man humbleth himself not, therefore, forgive him not.

10 O ye wicked ones, enter into the rock, and [ahide](#note10a) thee in the dust, for the fear of the Lord and the glory of his majesty shall smite thee.

11 And it shall come to pass that the [alofty](#note11a) looks of man shall be humbled, and the haughtiness of men shall be bowed down, and the Lord alone shall be exalted in that day.

12 For the [aday](#note12a) of the Lord of Hosts soon cometh upon all nations, yea, upon every one; yea, upon the [bproud](#note12b) and lofty, and upon every one who is lifted up, and he shall be brought low.

13 Yea, and the day of the Lord shall come upon all the [acedars](#note13a) of Lebanon, for they are high and lifted up; and upon all the oaks of Bashan;

14 And upon all the [ahigh](#note14a) mountains, and upon all the hills, and upon all the nations which are lifted up, and upon every people;

15 And upon every [ahigh](#note15a) tower, and upon every fenced wall;

16 And upon all the ships of the [asea](#note16a), and upon all the ships of Tarshish, and upon all pleasant pictures.

17 And the loftiness of man shall be bowed down, and the [ahaughtiness](#note17a) of men shall be made low; and the Lord alone shall be exalted in [bthat day](#note17b).

18 And the idols he shall utterly abolish.

19 And they shall go into the holes of the rocks, and into the caves of the earth, for the fear of the Lord shall come upon them and the [aglory](#note19a) of his majesty shall smite them, when he ariseth to shake terribly the earth.

20 In that day a man shall cast his idols of silver, and his idols of gold, which he hath made for himself to worship, to the moles and to the bats;

21 To go into the clefts of the rocks, and into the tops of the ragged rocks, for the fear of the Lord shall come upon them and the majesty of his glory shall smite them, when he ariseth to shake terribly the earth.

22 Cease ye from man, whose breath is in his nostrils; for wherein is he to be accounted of?

Chapter 13

Judah and Jerusalem will be punished for their disobedience—The Lord pleads for and judges His people—The daughters of Zion are cursed and tormented for their worldliness—Compare Isaiah 3. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aFor](#note1a) behold, the Lord, the Lord of Hosts, doth take away from Jerusalem, and from Judah, the stay and the staff, the whole staff of bread, and the whole stay of water—

2 The [amighty](#note2a) man, and the man of [bwar](#note2b), the judge, and the prophet, and the [cprudent](#note2c), and the ancient;

3 The captain of fifty, and the honorable man, and the counselor, and the cunning artificer, and the eloquent orator.

4 And I will give children unto them to be their princes, and babes shall rule over them.

5 And the people shall be [aoppressed](#note5a), every one by another, and every one by his neighbor; the child shall behave himself [bproudly](#note5b) against the ancient, and the base against the honorable.

6 When a man shall take hold of his brother of the house of his father, and shall say: Thou hast clothing, be thou our ruler, and let not this [aruin](#note6a) come under thy hand—

7 In that day shall he swear, saying: I will not be a healer; for in my house there is neither bread nor clothing; make me not a ruler of the people.

8 For Jerusalem is [aruined](#note8a), and Judah is [bfallen](#note8b), because their [ctongues](#note8c) and their doings have been against the Lord, to [dprovoke](#note8d) the eyes of his glory.

9 The show of their countenance doth witness against them, and doth declare their [asin](#note9a) to be even as [bSodom](#note9b), and they cannot hide it. Wo unto their souls, for they have rewarded evil unto themselves!

10 Say unto the righteous that it is [awell](#note10a) with them; for they shall [beat](#note10b) the fruit of their doings.

11 Wo unto the wicked, for they shall perish; for the reward of their hands shall be upon them!

12 And my people, children are their oppressors, and women rule over them. O my people, they who [alead](#note12a) thee cause thee to err and destroy the way of thy paths.

13 The Lord standeth up to [aplead](#note13a), and standeth to judge the people.

14 The Lord will enter into [ajudgment](#note14a) with the ancients of his people and the princes thereof; for ye have eaten up the [bvineyard](#note14b) and the spoil of the [cpoor](#note14c) in your houses.

15 What mean ye? Ye [abeat](#note15a) my people to pieces, and grind the faces of the poor, saith the Lord God of Hosts.

16 Moreover, the Lord saith: Because the daughters of Zion are [ahaughty](#note16a), and [bwalk](#note16b) with stretched-forth necks and wanton eyes, walking and mincing as they go, and making a tinkling with their feet—

17 Therefore the Lord will smite with a [ascab](#note17a) the crown of the head of the daughters of Zion, and the Lord will [bdiscover](#note17b) their secret parts.

18 In that [aday](#note18a) the Lord will take away the bravery of their tinkling ornaments, and cauls, and round tires like the moon;

19 The chains and the bracelets, and the mufflers;

20 The bonnets, and the ornaments of the legs, and the headbands, and the tablets, and the ear-rings;

21 The rings, and nose jewels;

22 The changeable suits of apparel, and the mantles, and the wimples, and the crisping-pins;

23 The glasses, and the fine linen, and hoods, and the veils.

24 And it shall come to pass, instead of sweet smell there shall be stink; and instead of a girdle, a rent; and instead of well set hair, [abaldness](#note24a); and instead of a stomacher, a girding of sackcloth; [bburning](#note24b) instead of [cbeauty](#note24c).

25 Thy men shall fall by the sword and thy mighty in the war.

26 And her [agates](#note26a) shall lament and [bmourn](#note26b); and she shall be desolate, and shall [csit](#note26c) upon the ground.

Chapter 14

Zion and her daughters will be redeemed and cleansed in the millennial day—Compare Isaiah 4. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) in that day, seven women shall take hold of one man, saying: We will eat our own bread, and wear our own apparel; only let us be called by thy name to take away our [breproach](#note1b).

2 In that day shall the [abranch](#note2a) of the Lord be beautiful and glorious; the fruit of the earth excellent and comely to them that are escaped of Israel.

3 And it shall come to pass, they that are [aleft](#note3a) in Zion and remain in Jerusalem shall be called holy, every one that is written among the living in Jerusalem—

4 When the Lord shall have [awashed](#note4a) away the filth of the daughters of Zion, and shall have purged the blood of Jerusalem from the midst thereof by the spirit of judgment and by the spirit of [bburning](#note4b).

5 And the [aLord](#note5a) will create upon every dwelling-place of mount Zion, and upon her assemblies, a [bcloud](#note5b) and smoke by day and the shining of a flaming fire by night; for upon all the glory of Zion shall be a defence.

6 And there shall be a tabernacle for a shadow in the daytime from the heat, and for a place of [arefuge](#note6a), and a covert from storm and from rain.

Chapter 15

The Lord’s vineyard (Israel) will become desolate, and His people will be scattered—Woes will come upon them in their apostate and scattered state—The Lord will lift an ensign and gather Israel—Compare Isaiah 5. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) then will I sing to my well-beloved a song of my beloved, touching his [bvineyard](#note1b). My well-beloved hath a vineyard in a very fruitful hill.

2 And he fenced it, and gathered out the stones thereof, and planted it with the choicest [avine](#note2a), and built a tower in the midst of it, and also made a wine-press therein; and he looked that it should bring forth grapes, and it brought forth wild grapes.

3 And now, O inhabitants of Jerusalem, and men of Judah, judge, I pray you, betwixt me and my vineyard.

4 What could have been done more to my vineyard that I have not done in it? Wherefore, when I looked that it should bring forth grapes it brought forth wild grapes.

5 And now go to; I will tell you what I will do to my vineyard—I will [atake away](#note5a) the hedge thereof, and it shall be eaten up; and I will break down the wall thereof, and it shall be trodden down;

6 And I will lay it waste; it shall not be pruned nor digged; but there shall come up [abriers](#note6a) and thorns; I will also command the clouds that they [brain](#note6b) no rain upon it.

7 For the [avineyard](#note7a) of the Lord of Hosts is the house of Israel, and the men of Judah his pleasant plant; and he looked for [bjudgment](#note7b), and behold, [coppression](#note7c); for righteousness, but behold, a cry.

8 Wo unto them that join [ahouse to house](#note8a), till there can be no place, that they may be placed alone in the midst of the earth!

9 In mine ears, said the Lord of Hosts, of a truth many houses shall be desolate, and great and fair cities without inhabitant.

10 Yea, ten acres of vineyard shall yield one [abath](#note10a), and the seed of a homer shall yield an ephah.

11 Wo unto them that rise up early in the morning, that they may [afollow](#note11a) strong drink, that continue until night, and [bwine](#note11b) inflame them!

12 And the harp, and the [aviol](#note12a), the tabret, and pipe, and wine are in their feasts; but they [bregard](#note12b) not the work of the Lord, neither consider the operation of his hands.

13 Therefore, my people are gone into [acaptivity](#note13a), because they have no [bknowledge](#note13b); and their honorable men are famished, and their multitude dried up with thirst.

14 Therefore, hell hath enlarged herself, and opened her mouth without measure; and their glory, and their multitude, and their pomp, and he that rejoiceth, shall descend into it.

15 And the mean man shall be [abrought](#note15a) down, and the [bmighty](#note15b) man shall be humbled, and the eyes of the [clofty](#note15c) shall be humbled.

16 But the Lord of Hosts shall be exalted in [ajudgment](#note16a), and God that is holy shall be sanctified in righteousness.

17 Then shall the lambs feed after their manner, and the waste places of the [afat](#note17a) ones shall strangers eat.

18 Wo unto them that draw iniquity with cords of [avanity](#note18a), and sin as it were with a cart rope;

19 That say: Let him [amake](#note19a) speed, [bhasten](#note19b) his work, that we may [csee](#note19c) it; and let the counsel of the Holy One of Israel draw nigh and come, that we may know it.

20 Wo unto them that [acall](#note20a) [bevil](#note20b) good, and good evil, that put [cdarkness](#note20c) for light, and light for darkness, that put bitter for sweet, and sweet for bitter!

21 Wo unto the [awise](#note21a) in their own eyes and [bprudent](#note21b) in their own sight!

22 Wo unto the mighty to drink [awine](#note22a), and men of strength to mingle strong drink;

23 Who justify the wicked for [areward](#note23a), and take away the righteousness of the righteous from him!

24 Therefore, as the [afire](#note24a) devoureth the [bstubble](#note24b), and the flame consumeth the [cchaff](#note24c), their [droot](#note24d) shall be rottenness, and their blossoms shall go up as dust; because they have cast away the law of the Lord of Hosts, and [edespised](#note24e) the word of the Holy One of Israel.

25 Therefore, is the [aanger](#note25a) of the Lord kindled against his people, and he hath stretched forth his hand against them, and hath smitten them; and the hills did tremble, and their carcasses were torn in the midst of the streets. For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

26 And he will lift up an [aensign](#note26a) to the [bnations](#note26b) from far, and will hiss unto them from the [cend](#note26c) of the earth; and behold, they shall [dcome](#note26d) with speed swiftly; none shall be weary nor stumble among them.

27 None shall slumber nor sleep; neither shall the girdle of their loins be loosed, nor the latchet of their shoes be broken;

28 Whose arrows shall be sharp, and all their bows bent, and their horses’ hoofs shall be counted like flint, and their wheels like a whirlwind, their roaring like a lion.

29 They shall roar like young [alions](#note29a); yea, they shall roar, and lay hold of the prey, and shall carry away safe, and none shall deliver.

30 And in that [aday](#note30a) they shall roar against them like the roaring of the sea; and if they look unto the land, behold, darkness and sorrow, and the light is darkened in the heavens thereof.

Chapter 16

Isaiah sees the Lord—Isaiah’s sins are forgiven—He is called to prophesy—He prophesies of the rejection by the Jews of Christ’s teachings—A remnant will return—Compare Isaiah 6. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aIn](#note1a) the [byear](#note1b) that king Uzziah died, I [csaw](#note1c) also the Lord sitting upon a throne, high and lifted up, and his train filled the temple.

2 Above it stood the [aseraphim](#note2a); each one had six wings; with twain he covered his face, and with twain he covered his feet, and with twain he did fly.

3 And one cried unto another, and said: Holy, holy, holy, is the Lord of Hosts; the whole earth is full of his [aglory](#note3a).

4 And the posts of the door moved at the voice of him that cried, and the house was filled with smoke.

5 Then said I: Wo is unto me! for I am undone; because I am a man of unclean lips; and I dwell in the midst of a people of unclean lips; for mine eyes have [aseen](#note5a) the King, the Lord of Hosts.

6 Then flew one of the seraphim unto me, having a live coal in his hand, which he had taken with the tongs from off the altar;

7 And he laid it upon my mouth, and said: Lo, this has touched thy lips; and thine [ainiquity](#note7a) is taken away, and thy sin purged.

8 Also I heard the voice of the Lord, saying: [aWhom](#note8a) shall I send, and who will go for us? Then I said: Here am I; send me.

9 And he said: Go and tell this people—Hear ye indeed, but they understood not; and see ye indeed, but they perceived not.

10 Make the heart of this people fat, and make their ears heavy, and shut their eyes—lest they see with their eyes, and [ahear](#note10a) with their ears, and understand with their [bheart](#note10b), and be converted and be healed.

11 Then said I: Lord, how long? And he said: Until the cities be wasted without inhabitant, and the houses without man, and the land be utterly desolate;

12 And the Lord have [aremoved](#note12a) men far away, for there shall be a great forsaking in the midst of the land.

13 But yet there shall be a tenth, and they shall return, and shall be eaten, as a teil tree, and as an oak whose substance is in them when they cast their leaves; so the [aholy seed](#note13a) shall be the substance thereof.

Chapter 17

Ephraim and Syria wage war against Judah—Christ will be born of a virgin—Compare Isaiah 7. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) it came to pass in the days of [bAhaz](#note1b) the son of [cJotham](#note1c), the son of Uzziah, king of Judah, that [dRezin](#note1d), king of Syria, and [ePekah](#note1e) the son of Remaliah, king of Israel, went up toward Jerusalem to war against it, but could not prevail against it.

2 And it was told the house of David, saying: Syria is confederate with Ephraim. And his heart was moved, and the heart of his people, as the trees of the wood are moved with the wind.

3 Then said the Lord unto Isaiah: Go forth now to meet Ahaz, thou and Shearjashub thy son, at the end of the [aconduit](#note3a) of the upper pool in the highway of the fuller’s field;

4 And say unto him: Take heed, and be quiet; fear not, neither be faint-hearted for the two tails of these smoking firebrands, for the fierce anger of Rezin with Syria, and of the son of Remaliah.

5 Because Syria, Ephraim, and the son of Remaliah, have taken evil counsel against thee, saying:

6 Let us go up against Judah and vex it, and let us make a breach therein for us, and set a king in the midst of it, yea, the son of Tabeal.

7 Thus saith the Lord God: [aIt](#note7a) shall not stand, neither shall it come to pass.

8 For the head of Syria is Damascus, and the head of Damascus, Rezin; and within threescore and five years shall Ephraim be [abroken](#note8a) that it be not a people.

9 And the head of Ephraim is Samaria, and the head of Samaria is Remaliah’s son. If ye will [anot believe](#note9a) surely ye shall not be established.

10 Moreover, the Lord spake again unto Ahaz, saying:

11 Ask thee a [asign](#note11a) of the Lord thy God; ask it either in the depths, or in the heights above.

12 But Ahaz said: I will not ask, neither will I [atempt](#note12a) the Lord.

13 And he said: Hear ye now, O house of David; is it a small thing for you to weary men, but will ye weary my God also?

14 Therefore, the Lord himself shall give you a sign—Behold, a [avirgin](#note14a) shall conceive, and shall bear a son, and shall call his name [bImmanuel](#note14b).

15 Butter and [ahoney](#note15a) shall he eat, that he may know to refuse the evil and to choose the good.

16 For [abefore](#note16a) the child shall know to refuse the evil and choose the good, the land that thou abhorrest shall be forsaken of [bboth](#note16b) her kings.

17 The Lord shall [abring](#note17a) upon thee, and upon thy people, and upon thy father’s house, days that have not come from the day that [bEphraim](#note17b) departed from Judah, the king of Assyria.

18 And it shall come to pass in that day that the Lord shall hiss for the fly that is in the uttermost part of Egypt, and for the bee that is in the land of Assyria.

19 And they shall come, and shall rest all of them in the desolate valleys, and in the holes of the rocks, and upon all thorns, and upon all bushes.

20 In the same day shall the Lord shave with a [arazor](#note20a) that is hired, by them beyond the river, by the king of Assyria, the head, and the hair of the feet; and it shall also consume the beard.

21 And it shall come to pass in that day, a man shall nourish a young cow and two sheep;

22 And it shall come to pass, for the abundance of milk they shall give he shall eat butter; for butter and honey shall every one eat that is left in the land.

23 And it shall come to pass in that day, every place shall be, where there were a thousand vines at a thousand silverlings, which shall be for briers and thorns.

24 With arrows and with bows shall men come thither, because all the land shall become briers and thorns.

25 And all hills that shall be digged with the mattock, there shall not come thither the fear of briers and thorns; but it shall be for the sending forth of oxen, and the treading of lesser cattle.

Chapter 18

Christ will be as a stone of stumbling and a rock of offense—Seek the Lord, not peeping wizards—Turn to the law and to the testimony for guidance—Compare Isaiah 8. About 559–545 B.C.

1 Moreover, the word of the Lord said unto me: Take thee a great [aroll](#note1a), and write in it with a man’s pen, concerning [bMaher-shalal-hash-baz](#note1b).

2 And I took unto me faithful [awitnesses](#note2a) to record, Uriah the priest, and Zechariah the son of Jeberechiah.

3 And I went unto the prophetess; and she conceived and bare a son. Then said the Lord to me: [aCall](#note3a) his name, Maher-shalal-hash-baz.

4 For behold, [athe child](#note4a) shall [bnot](#note4b) have knowledge to cry, My father, and my mother, before the riches of Damascus and the [cspoil](#note4c) of [dSamaria](#note4d) shall be taken away before the king of [eAssyria](#note4e).

5 The Lord spake also unto me again, saying:

6 Forasmuch as this people refuseth the waters of [aShiloah](#note6a) that go softly, and rejoice in [bRezin](#note6b) and Remaliah’s son;

7 Now therefore, behold, the Lord bringeth up upon them the waters of the river, strong and many, even the king of [aAssyria](#note7a) and all his glory; and he shall come up over all his channels, and go over all his banks.

8 And he shall pass through Judah; he shall overflow and go over, he shall [areach](#note8a) even to the neck; and the stretching out of his wings shall fill the breadth of thy land, O Immanuel.

9 [aAssociate](#note9a) yourselves, O ye people, and ye shall be broken in pieces; and give ear all ye of far countries; gird yourselves, and ye shall be broken in pieces; gird yourselves, and ye shall be broken in pieces.

10 Take counsel together, and it shall come to naught; speak the word, and it shall not stand; for God is with us.

11 For the Lord spake thus to me with a strong hand, and instructed me that I should not walk in the way of this people, saying:

12 Say ye not, A confederacy, to all to whom this people shall say, A [aconfederacy](#note12a); neither fear ye their fear, nor be afraid.

13 Sanctify the Lord of Hosts himself, and let him be your fear, and let him be your dread.

14 And he shall be for a sanctuary; but for a [astone](#note14a) of [bstumbling](#note14b), and for a [crock](#note14c) of [doffense](#note14d) to both the houses of Israel, for a gin and a [esnare](#note14e) to the inhabitants of Jerusalem.

15 And many among them shall [astumble](#note15a) and fall, and be broken, and be snared, and be taken.

16 [aBind](#note16a) up the testimony, seal the law among my disciples.

17 And I will wait upon the Lord, that [ahideth](#note17a) his face from the house of Jacob, and I will look for him.

18 Behold, I and the children whom the Lord hath given me are for [asigns](#note18a) and for wonders in Israel from the Lord of Hosts, which dwelleth in Mount Zion.

19 And when they shall say unto you: Seek unto them that have [afamiliar spirits](#note19a), and unto [bwizards](#note19b) that peep and mutter—[cshould not](#note19c) a people seek unto their God for the living to hear from the dead?

20 To the [alaw](#note20a) and to the testimony; and if they speak not according to this word, it is because there is no light in them.

21 And they shall pass through it hardly bestead and hungry; and it shall come to pass that when they shall be hungry, they shall fret themselves, and curse their king and their God, and look upward.

22 And they shall look unto the earth and behold trouble, and [adarkness](#note22a), dimness of anguish, and shall be driven to darkness.

Chapter 19

Isaiah speaks messianically—The people in darkness will see a great light—Unto us a child is born—He will be the Prince of Peace and will reign on David’s throne—Compare Isaiah 9. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aNevertheless](#note1a), the dimness shall not be such as was in her vexation, when at first he lightly afflicted the [bland](#note1b) of [cZebulun](#note1c), and the land of [dNaphtali](#note1d), and afterwards did more grievously afflict by the way of the Red Sea beyond Jordan in Galilee of the nations.

2 The people that walked in darkness have seen a great light; they that dwell in the land of the shadow of death, upon them hath the light shined.

3 Thou hast multiplied the nation, and [aincreased](#note3a) the joy—they joy before thee according to the joy in harvest, and as men rejoice when they divide the spoil.

4 For thou hast broken the yoke of [ahis](#note4a) burden, and the staff of his shoulder, the rod of his [boppressor](#note4b).

5 For every battle of the warrior is with confused noise, and garments rolled in blood; but [athis](#note5a) shall be with burning and fuel of fire.

6 For unto us a [achild](#note6a) is born, unto us a son is given; and the [bgovernment](#note6b) shall be upon his shoulder; and his name shall be called, Wonderful, Counselor, The [cMighty God](#note6c), The [dEverlasting Father](#note6d), The Prince of [ePeace](#note6e).

7 Of the increase of [agovernment](#note7a) and peace [bthere](#note7b) is no end, upon the throne of [cDavid](#note7c), and upon his kingdom to order it, and to establish it with judgment and with justice from henceforth, even forever. The zeal of the Lord of Hosts will perform this.

8 The Lord sent his word unto Jacob and it hath lighted upon Israel.

9 And all the people shall know, even Ephraim and the inhabitants of Samaria, that say in the pride and stoutness of heart:

10 The bricks are fallen down, but we will build with hewn [astones](#note10a); the sycamores are cut down, but we will change them into [bcedars](#note10b).

11 Therefore the Lord shall set up the adversaries of [aRezin](#note11a) against him, and join his enemies together;

12 The Syrians before and the Philistines behind; and they shall [adevour](#note12a) Israel with open mouth. For all this his [banger](#note12b) is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

13 For the people turneth not unto [ahim](#note13a) that smiteth them, neither do they seek the Lord of Hosts.

14 Therefore will the Lord cut off from Israel head and tail, branch and rush [ain](#note14a) one day.

15 The [aancient](#note15a), he is the head; and the prophet that teacheth lies, he is the tail.

16 For the [aleaders](#note16a) of this people cause them to err; and they that are [bled](#note16b) of them are destroyed.

17 Therefore the Lord shall have no joy in their young men, neither shall have [amercy](#note17a) on their fatherless and [bwidows](#note17b); for [cevery](#note17c) one of them is a hypocrite and an [devildoer](#note17d), and every mouth speaketh [efolly](#note17e). For all this his anger is not turned away, but his [fhand](#note17f) is stretched out still.

18 For [awickedness](#note18a) burneth as the fire; it shall devour the briers and thorns, and shall kindle in the thickets of the forests, and they shall mount up like the lifting up of smoke.

19 Through the wrath of the Lord of Hosts is the [aland](#note19a) darkened, and the people shall be as the fuel of the fire; [bno man](#note19b) shall spare his brother.

20 And he [ashall](#note20a) snatch on the right hand and be hungry; and he shall [beat](#note20b) on the left hand and they shall not be satisfied; they shall eat every man the flesh of his own arm—

21 Manasseh, [aEphraim](#note21a); and Ephraim, Manasseh; they together shall be against [bJudah](#note21b). For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

Chapter 20

The destruction of Assyria is a type of the destruction of the wicked at the Second Coming—Few people will be left after the Lord comes again—The remnant of Jacob will return in that day—Compare Isaiah 10. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aWo](#note1a) unto them that decree [bunrighteous](#note1b) decrees, and that write grievousness which they have prescribed;

2 To turn away the needy from judgment, and to take away the right from the [apoor](#note2a) of my people, that [bwidows](#note2b) may be their prey, and that they may rob the fatherless!

3 And what will ye do in the day of visitation, and in the desolation which shall come from far? to whom will ye flee for help? and where will ye leave your glory?

4 Without me they shall bow down under the prisoners, and they shall fall under the slain. For all this his anger is not turned away, but his hand is stretched out still.

5 O Assyrian, the rod of mine anger, and the staff in their hand is [atheir](#note5a) indignation.

6 I will send him [aagainst a hypocritical nation](#note6a), and against the people of my wrath will I give him a charge to take the spoil, and to take the prey, and to tread them down like the mire of the streets.

7 Howbeit he meaneth not so, neither doth his heart think so; but in his heart it is to destroy and cut off nations not a few.

8 For he saith: Are not my [aprinces](#note8a) altogether kings?

9 Is not [aCalno](#note9a) as [bCarchemish](#note9b)? Is not Hamath as Arpad? Is not Samaria as [cDamascus](#note9c)?

10 As [amy hand](#note10a) hath founded the kingdoms of the idols, and whose graven images did excel them of Jerusalem and of Samaria;

11 Shall I not, as I have done unto Samaria and her [aidols](#note11a), so do to Jerusalem and to her idols?

12 Wherefore it shall come to pass that when the Lord hath performed his whole work upon Mount Zion and upon Jerusalem, I will punish the fruit of the stout heart of the king of [aAssyria](#note12a), and the glory of his high looks.

13 For [ahe](#note13a) saith: By the strength of [bmy hand](#note13b) and by my wisdom I have done these things; for I am prudent; and I have moved the borders of the people, and have robbed their treasures, and I have put down the inhabitants like a valiant man;

14 And my hand hath found as a nest the riches of the people; and as one gathereth eggs that are left have I gathered all the earth; and there was none that moved the wing, or opened the mouth, or peeped.

15 Shall the [aax](#note15a) boast itself against him that heweth therewith? Shall the saw magnify itself against him that shaketh it? As if the rod should shake itself against them that lift it up, or as if the staff should lift up itself as if it were no wood!

16 Therefore shall the Lord, the Lord of Hosts, send among his fat ones, leanness; and under his glory he shall kindle a burning like the burning of a fire.

17 And the light of Israel shall be for a [afire](#note17a), and his Holy One for a flame, and shall burn and shall devour his thorns and his briers in one day;

18 And shall consume the glory of his forest, and of his fruitful field, both soul and body; and they shall be as when a standard-bearer fainteth.

19 And the [arest](#note19a) of the trees of his forest shall be few, that a child may write them.

20 And it shall come to pass in that day, that the remnant of Israel, and such as are escaped of the [ahouse of Jacob](#note20a), shall no more again [bstay upon](#note20b) him that smote them, but shall stay upon the Lord, the Holy One of Israel, in truth.

21 The [aremnant](#note21a) shall return, yea, even the remnant of Jacob, unto the mighty God.

22 For though thy people [aIsrael](#note22a) be as the sand of the sea, yet a remnant of them shall [breturn](#note22b); the [cconsumption](#note22c) decreed shall overflow with righteousness.

23 For the Lord God of Hosts shall make a [aconsumption](#note23a), even determined in all the land.

24 Therefore, thus saith the Lord God of Hosts: O my people that dwellest in Zion, [abe](#note24a) not afraid of the Assyrian; he shall smite thee with a rod, and shall lift up his staff against thee, after the [bmanner](#note24b) of Egypt.

25 For yet a very little while, and the [aindignation](#note25a) shall cease, and mine anger in their destruction.

26 And the Lord of Hosts shall [astir up](#note26a) a scourge for him according to the slaughter of [bMidian](#note26b) at the rock of Oreb; and as his rod was upon the sea so shall he lift it up after the manner of [cEgypt](#note26c).

27 And it shall come to pass in that day that his [aburden](#note27a) shall be taken away from off thy shoulder, and his yoke from off thy neck, and the yoke shall be destroyed because of the [banointing](#note27b).

28 [aHe](#note28a) is come to Aiath, he is passed to Migron; at Michmash he hath laid up his carriages.

29 They are gone over the [apassage](#note29a); they have taken up their lodging at [bGeba](#note29b); Ramath is afraid; [cGibeah](#note29c) of Saul is fled.

30 Lift up the voice, O daughter of [aGallim](#note30a); cause it to be heard unto Laish, O poor [bAnathoth](#note30b).

31 Madmenah is removed; the inhabitants of Gebim gather themselves to flee.

32 As yet shall he remain at [aNob](#note32a) that day; he shall shake his hand against the mount of the daughter of Zion, the hill of Jerusalem.

33 Behold, the Lord, the Lord of Hosts shall lop the bough with terror; and the [ahigh](#note33a) ones of stature shall be [bhewn](#note33b) down; and the [chaughty](#note33c) shall be humbled.

34 And he shall cut down the thickets of the forests with iron, and Lebanon shall fall by a mighty one.

Chapter 21

The stem of Jesse (Christ) will judge in righteousness—The knowledge of God will cover the earth in the Millennium—The Lord will raise an ensign and gather Israel—Compare Isaiah 11. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) there shall [bcome](#note1b) forth a rod out of the [cstem of Jesse](#note1c), and a [dbranch](#note1d) shall grow out of his roots.

2 And the [aSpirit](#note2a) of the Lord shall rest upon him, the spirit of [bwisdom](#note2b) and [cunderstanding](#note2c), the spirit of counsel and might, the spirit of knowledge and of the fear of the Lord;

3 And shall make him of quick understanding in the fear of the Lord; and he shall not [ajudge](#note3a) after the sight of his eyes, neither reprove after the hearing of his ears.

4 But with [arighteousness](#note4a) shall he [bjudge](#note4b) the poor, and reprove with equity for the [cmeek](#note4c) of the earth; and he shall [dsmite](#note4d) the earth with the [erod](#note4e) of his mouth, and with the breath of his lips shall he slay the wicked.

5 And [arighteousness](#note5a) shall be the girdle of his loins, and faithfulness the girdle of his reins.

6 The [awolf](#note6a) also shall dwell with the lamb, and the leopard shall lie down with the kid, and the calf and the young lion and fatling together; and a little child shall lead them.

7 And the cow and the bear shall feed; their young ones shall lie down together; and the lion shall eat straw like the ox.

8 And the sucking child shall play on the hole of the asp, and the weaned child shall put his hand on the cockatrice’s den.

9 They shall [anot](#note9a) hurt nor [bdestroy](#note9b) in all my holy mountain, for the [cearth](#note9c) shall be full of the [dknowledge](#note9d) of the Lord, as the waters cover the sea.

10 And in that day there shall be a [aroot of Jesse](#note10a), which shall stand for an ensign of the people; to it shall the [bGentiles](#note10b) seek; and his [crest](#note10c) shall be glorious.

11 And it shall come to pass in that day that the Lord shall set his hand again the [asecond](#note11a) time to recover the remnant of his people which shall be left, from [bAssyria](#note11b), and from Egypt, and from Pathros, and from Cush, and from Elam, and from [cShinar](#note11c), and from Hamath, and from the islands of the sea.

12 And he shall set up an [aensign](#note12a) for the nations, and shall assemble the [boutcasts](#note12b) of Israel, and [cgather](#note12c) together the dispersed of Judah from the four corners of the earth.

13 The [aenvy](#note13a) of Ephraim also shall depart, and the adversaries of Judah shall be cut off; Ephraim shall not [benvy](#note13b) [cJudah](#note13c), and Judah shall not vex Ephraim.

14 But they shall fly upon the shoulders of the [aPhilistines](#note14a) towards the west; they shall spoil them of the east together; they shall lay their hand upon [bEdom](#note14b) and [cMoab](#note14c); and the children of Ammon shall obey them.

15 And the Lord shall utterly [adestroy](#note15a) the tongue of the Egyptian sea; and with his mighty wind he shall shake his hand over the river, and shall smite it in the seven streams, and make men go over [bdry](#note15b) shod.

16 And there shall be a [ahighway](#note16a) for the remnant of his people which shall be left, from Assyria, like as it was to Israel in the day that he came up out of the land of Egypt.

Chapter 22

In the millennial day all men will praise the Lord—He will dwell among them—Compare Isaiah 12. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aAnd](#note1a) in that day thou shalt say: O Lord, I will praise thee; though thou wast angry with me thine anger is turned away, and thou comfortedst me.

2 Behold, God is my salvation; I will [atrust](#note2a), and not be afraid; for the Lord [bJehovah](#note2b) is my [cstrength](#note2c) and my [dsong](#note2d); he also has become my salvation.

3 Therefore, with joy shall ye draw [awater](#note3a) out of the wells of salvation.

4 And in that day shall ye say: [aPraise](#note4a) the Lord, call upon his name, declare his doings among the people, make mention that his name is exalted.

5 [aSing](#note5a) unto the Lord; for he hath done excellent things; this is known in all the earth.

6 [aCry](#note6a) out and shout, thou inhabitant of Zion; for great is the Holy One of Israel in the midst of thee.

Chapter 23

The destruction of Babylon is a type of the destruction at the Second Coming—It will be a day of wrath and vengeance—Babylon (the world) will fall forever—Compare Isaiah 13. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aThe burden](#note1a) of [bBabylon](#note1b), which Isaiah the son of Amoz did see.

2 Lift ye up a banner upon the high mountain, exalt the voice unto them, [ashake the hand](#note2a), that they may go into the gates of the nobles.

3 I have commanded my sanctified ones, I have also called my [amighty](#note3a) ones, for mine anger is not upon them that rejoice in my highness.

4 The noise of the multitude in the mountains like as of a great people, a tumultuous noise of the [akingdoms](#note4a) of nations [bgathered](#note4b) together, the Lord of Hosts mustereth the hosts of the battle.

5 They come from a far country, from the end of heaven, yea, the Lord, and the weapons of his indignation, to destroy the whole land.

6 Howl ye, for the [aday](#note6a) of the Lord is at hand; it shall come as a destruction from the Almighty.

7 Therefore shall all hands be faint, every man’s heart shall [amelt](#note7a);

8 And they shall be afraid; pangs and sorrows shall take hold of them; they shall be amazed one at another; their faces shall be as flames.

9 Behold, the day of the Lord cometh, cruel both with wrath and fierce anger, to lay the land desolate; and he shall [adestroy](#note9a) the sinners thereof out of it.

10 For the [astars](#note10a) of heaven and the [bconstellations](#note10b) thereof shall not give their [clight](#note10c); the [dsun](#note10d) shall be darkened in his going forth, and the moon shall not cause her light to shine.

11 And I will [apunish](#note11a) the world for evil, and the [bwicked](#note11b) for their iniquity; I will cause the arrogancy of the [cproud](#note11c) to cease, and will lay down the haughtiness of the terrible.

12 I will make a [aman](#note12a) more precious than fine gold; even a man than the golden wedge of Ophir.

13 Therefore, I will [ashake](#note13a) the heavens, and the earth shall [bremove](#note13b) out of her place, in the wrath of the Lord of Hosts, and in the day of his fierce anger.

14 And it shall be as the chased roe, and as a sheep that no man taketh up; and they shall every man turn to his own people, and flee every one into his own [aland](#note14a).

15 Every one that is proud shall be thrust through; yea, and every one that is [ajoined](#note15a) to the wicked shall fall by the sword.

16 Their [achildren](#note16a) also shall be [bdashed](#note16b) to pieces before their eyes; their houses shall be spoiled and their wives ravished.

17 Behold, I will stir up the [aMedes](#note17a) against them, which shall not regard silver and gold, nor shall they delight in it.

18 Their bows shall also dash the young men to pieces; and they shall have no [apity](#note18a) on the fruit of the womb; their eyes shall not spare children.

19 And [aBabylon](#note19a), the glory of kingdoms, the beauty of the Chaldees’ excellency, shall be as when God overthrew [bSodom](#note19b) and Gomorrah.

20 It shall never be [ainhabited](#note20a), neither shall it be dwelt in from generation to generation: neither shall the Arabian pitch tent there; neither shall the shepherds make their fold there.

21 But [awild](#note21a) beasts of the desert shall lie there; and their houses shall be full of doleful creatures; and owls shall dwell there, and satyrs shall dance there.

22 And the wild beasts of the islands shall cry in their desolate houses, and dragons in their pleasant palaces; and her time is near to come, and her day shall not be prolonged. For I will destroy her speedily; yea, for I will be merciful unto my people, but the wicked shall perish.

* [◀](#ldsBACK_note21a)

  21a

  Isa. 34:14 (11–15).

Chapter 24

Israel will be gathered and will enjoy millennial rest—Lucifer was cast out of heaven for rebellion—Israel will triumph over Babylon (the world)—Compare Isaiah 14. About 559–545 B.C.

1 [aFor](#note1a) the Lord will have mercy on Jacob, and will yet [bchoose](#note1b) Israel, and set them in their own land; and the [cstrangers](#note1c) shall be joined with them, and they shall cleave to the house of Jacob.

2 And the people shall take them and bring them to their place; yea, from far unto the ends of the earth; and they shall return to their [alands of promise](#note2a). And the house of Israel shall [bpossess](#note2b) them, and the land of the Lord shall be for [cservants](#note2c) and handmaids; and they shall take them captives unto whom they were captives; and they shall [drule](#note2d) over their oppressors.

3 And it shall come to pass in that day that the Lord shall give thee [arest](#note3a), from thy sorrow, and from thy fear, and from the hard bondage wherein thou wast made to serve.

4 And it shall come to pass in that day, that thou shalt take up this proverb [aagainst](#note4a) the king of [bBabylon](#note4b), and say: How hath the oppressor ceased, the golden city ceased!

5 The Lord hath broken the staff of the [awicked](#note5a), the scepters of the rulers.

6 [aHe](#note6a) who smote the people in wrath with a continual stroke, he that ruled the nations in anger, is persecuted, and none hindereth.

7 The whole earth is at [arest](#note7a), and is quiet; they break forth into [bsinging](#note7b).

8 Yea, the fir trees rejoice at thee, and also the cedars of Lebanon, saying: Since thou art laid down no feller is come up against us.

9 [aHell](#note9a) from beneath is moved for thee to meet thee at thy coming; it stirreth up the [bdead](#note9b) for thee, even all the chief ones of the earth; it hath raised up from their thrones all the kings of the nations.

10 All they shall speak and say unto thee: Art thou also become weak as we? Art thou become like unto us?

11 Thy pomp is brought down to the grave; the noise of thy viols is not heard; the worm is spread under thee, and the worms cover thee.

12 [aHow](#note12a) art thou fallen from heaven, O [bLucifer](#note12b), son of the morning! Art thou cut down to the ground, which did weaken the nations!

13 For thou hast said in thy heart: [aI](#note13a) will ascend into heaven, I will exalt my throne above the stars of God; I will sit also upon the mount of the congregation, in the sides of the north;

14 [aI](#note14a) will ascend above the heights of the clouds; I will be like the Most High.

15 Yet thou shalt be brought down to hell, to the sides of the [apit](#note15a).

16 They that see thee shall narrowly look upon thee, and shall consider thee, and shall say: Is this the man that made the earth to tremble, that did shake kingdoms?

17 And made the world as a wilderness, and destroyed the cities thereof, and opened not the house of his prisoners?

18 All the kings of the nations, yea, all of them, lie in glory, every one of them in his own house.

19 But thou art cast out of thy grave like an abominable branch, and the remnant of those that are slain, thrust through with a sword, that go down to the stones of the pit; as a carcass trodden under feet.

20 Thou shalt not be joined with them in burial, because thou hast destroyed thy land and slain thy people; the [aseed](#note20a) of [bevil-doers](#note20b) shall never be renowned.

21 Prepare slaughter for his children for the [ainiquities](#note21a) of their fathers, that they do not rise, nor possess the land, nor fill the face of the world with cities.

22 For I will rise up against them, saith the Lord of Hosts, and cut off from Babylon the [aname](#note22a), and remnant, and son, and [bnephew](#note22b), saith the Lord.

23 I will also make it a [apossession](#note23a) for the bittern, and pools of water; and I will sweep it with the besom of destruction, saith the Lord of Hosts.

24 The Lord of Hosts hath sworn, saying: Surely as I have thought, so shall it come to pass; and as I have purposed, so shall it stand—

25 That I will bring the Assyrian in my land, and upon my mountains tread him under foot; then shall his [ayoke](#note25a) depart from off them, and his burden depart from off their shoulders.

26 This is the purpose that is purposed upon the whole earth; and this is the hand that is stretched out upon all nations.

27 For the Lord of Hosts hath purposed, and who shall disannul? And his hand is stretched out, and who shall turn it back?

28 In the year that king [aAhaz](#note28a) died was this burden.

29 Rejoice not thou, whole Palestina, because the rod of him that [asmote](#note29a) thee is broken; for out of the serpent’s root shall come forth a cockatrice, and his [bfruit](#note29b) shall be a [cfiery flying serpent](#note29c).

30 And the firstborn of the poor shall feed, and the needy shall lie down in safety; and I will kill thy root with famine, and he shall slay thy remnant.

31 Howl, O gate; cry, O city; thou, whole Palestina, art dissolved; for there shall come from the north a smoke, and none shall be alone in his appointed times.

32 What shall then answer the messengers of the nations? That the Lord hath founded [aZion](#note32a), and the [bpoor](#note32b) of his people shall trust in it.

Chapter 25

Nephi glories in plainness—Isaiah’s prophecies will be understood in the last days—The Jews will return from Babylon, crucify the Messiah, and be scattered and scourged—They will be restored when they believe in the Messiah—He will first come six hundred years after Lehi left Jerusalem—The Nephites keep the law of Moses and believe in Christ, who is the Holy One of Israel. About 559–545 B.C.

1 Now I, Nephi, do speak somewhat concerning the words which I have written, which have been spoken by the mouth of Isaiah. For behold, Isaiah spake many things which were [ahard](#note1a) for many of my people to understand; for they know not concerning the manner of prophesying among the Jews.

2 For I, Nephi, have not taught them many things concerning the manner of the Jews; for their [aworks](#note2a) were works of darkness, and their doings were doings of abominations.

3 Wherefore, I write unto my people, unto all those that shall receive hereafter these things which I write, [athat](#note3a) they may know the judgments of God, that they come upon all nations, according to the word which he hath spoken.

4 Wherefore, hearken, O my people, which are of the house of Israel, and give ear unto my words; for because the words of Isaiah are not plain unto you, nevertheless they are plain unto all those that are filled with the [aspirit](#note4a) of [bprophecy](#note4b). But I give unto you a [cprophecy](#note4c), according to the spirit which is in me; wherefore I shall prophesy according to the [dplainness](#note4d) which hath been with me from the time that I came out from Jerusalem with my father; for behold, my soul delighteth in [eplainness](#note4e) unto my people, that they may learn.

5 Yea, and my soul delighteth in the words of [aIsaiah](#note5a), for I came out from Jerusalem, and mine eyes hath beheld the things of the [bJews](#note5b), and I know that the Jews do [cunderstand](#note5c) the things of the prophets, and there is none other people that understand the things which were spoken unto the Jews like unto them, save it be that they are taught after the manner of the things of the Jews.

6 But behold, I, Nephi, have not taught my children after the manner of the Jews; but behold, I, of myself, have dwelt at Jerusalem, wherefore I know concerning the regions round about; and I have made mention unto my children concerning the judgments of God, which [ahath](#note6a) come to pass among the Jews, unto my children, according to all that which Isaiah hath spoken, and I do not write them.

7 But behold, I proceed with mine own prophecy, according to my [aplainness](#note7a); in the which I [bknow](#note7b) that no man can err; nevertheless, in the days that the prophecies of Isaiah shall be fulfilled men shall know of a surety, at the times when they shall come to pass.

8 Wherefore, they are of [aworth](#note8a) unto the children of men, and he that supposeth that they are not, unto them will I speak particularly, and confine the words unto mine [bown](#note8b) people; for I know that they shall be of great worth unto them in the [clast days](#note8c); for in that day shall they understand them; wherefore, for their good have I written them.

9 And as one generation hath been [adestroyed](#note9a) among the Jews because of iniquity, even so have they been destroyed from generation to generation according to their iniquities; and never hath any of them been destroyed save it were [bforetold](#note9b) them by the prophets of the Lord.

10 Wherefore, it hath been told them concerning the destruction which should come upon them, immediately after my father left [aJerusalem](#note10a); nevertheless, they [bhardened](#note10b) their hearts; and according to my prophecy they have been destroyed, save it be those which are [ccarried away](#note10c) [dcaptive](#note10d) into Babylon.

11 And now this I speak because of the [aspirit](#note11a) which is in me. And notwithstanding they have been carried away they shall return again, and possess the land of Jerusalem; wherefore, they shall be [brestored](#note11b) again to the [cland](#note11c) of their inheritance.

12 But, behold, they shall have [awars](#note12a), and rumors of wars; and when the day cometh that the [bOnly Begotten](#note12b) of the Father, yea, even the Father of heaven and of earth, shall [cmanifest](#note12c) himself unto them in the flesh, behold, they will reject him, because of their iniquities, and the hardness of their hearts, and the stiffness of their necks.

13 Behold, they will [acrucify](#note13a) him; and after he is laid in a [bsepulchre](#note13b) for the space of [cthree](#note13c) days he shall [drise](#note13d) from the dead, with healing in his wings; and all those who shall believe on his name shall be saved in the kingdom of God. Wherefore, my soul delighteth to prophesy concerning him, for I have [eseen](#note13e) his day, and my heart doth magnify his holy name.

14 And behold it shall come to pass that after the [aMessiah](#note14a) hath risen from the dead, and hath manifested himself unto his people, unto as many as will believe on his name, behold, Jerusalem shall be [bdestroyed](#note14b) again; for [cwo](#note14c) unto them that fight against God and the people of his [dchurch](#note14d).

15 Wherefore, the [aJews](#note15a) shall be [bscattered](#note15b) among all nations; yea, and also [cBabylon](#note15c) shall be destroyed; wherefore, the Jews shall be scattered by other nations.

16 And after they have been [ascattered](#note16a), and the Lord God hath scourged them by other nations for the space of many generations, yea, even down from generation to generation until they shall be persuaded to [bbelieve](#note16b) in Christ, the Son of God, and the atonement, which is infinite for all mankind—and when that day shall come that they shall believe in Christ, and worship the Father in his name, with pure hearts and [cclean hands](#note16c), and look not forward any more for [danother](#note16d) Messiah, then, at that time, the day will come that it must needs be expedient that they should believe these things.

17 And the Lord will set his hand again the second time to [arestore](#note17a) his people from their lost and fallen state. Wherefore, he will proceed to do a [bmarvelous work](#note17b) and a wonder among the children of men.

18 Wherefore, he shall bring forth [ahis](#note18a) [bwords](#note18b) unto them, which words shall [cjudge](#note18c) them at the last day, for they shall be given them for the purpose of [dconvincing](#note18d) them of the true Messiah, who was rejected by them; and unto the convincing of them that they need not look forward any more for a Messiah to come, for there should not any come, save it should be a [efalse Messiah](#note18e) which should deceive the people; for there is save one [fMessiah](#note18f) spoken of by the prophets, and that Messiah is he who should be rejected of the Jews.

19 For according to the words of the prophets, the [aMessiah](#note19a) cometh in [bsix hundred](#note19b) years from the time that my father left Jerusalem; and according to the words of the prophets, and also the word of the [cangel](#note19c) of God, his [dname](#note19d) shall be Jesus Christ, the [eSon of God](#note19e).

20 And now, my brethren, I have spoken plainly that ye cannot err. And as the Lord God liveth that [abrought](#note20a) Israel up out of the land of Egypt, and gave unto Moses power that he should [bheal](#note20b) the nations after they had been bitten by the poisonous serpents, if they would cast their eyes unto the [cserpent](#note20c) which he did raise up before them, and also gave him power that he should smite the [drock](#note20d) and the water should come forth; yea, behold I say unto you, that as these things are [etrue](#note20e), and as the Lord God liveth, there is none other [fname](#note20f) given under heaven save it be this Jesus Christ, of which I have spoken, whereby man can be saved.

21 Wherefore, for this cause hath the Lord God promised unto me that these things which I [awrite](#note21a) shall be kept and preserved, and handed down unto my seed, from generation to generation, that the promise may be fulfilled unto Joseph, that his seed should never [bperish](#note21b) as long as the earth should stand.

22 Wherefore, these things shall go from generation to generation as long as the earth shall stand; and they shall go according to the will and pleasure of God; and the nations who shall possess them shall be [ajudged](#note22a) of them according to the words which are written.

23 For we labor diligently to write, to [apersuade](#note23a) our children, and also our brethren, to believe in Christ, and to be reconciled to God; for we know that it is by [bgrace](#note23b) that we are saved, after all we can [cdo](#note23c).

24 And, notwithstanding we believe in Christ, we [akeep](#note24a) the law of Moses, and look forward with steadfastness unto Christ, until the law shall be fulfilled.

25 For, for this end was the [alaw](#note25a) given; wherefore the law hath become [bdead](#note25b) unto us, and we are made alive in Christ because of our faith; yet we keep the law because of the commandments.

26 And we [atalk](#note26a) of Christ, we rejoice in Christ, we preach of Christ, we [bprophesy](#note26b) of Christ, and we write according to our prophecies, that our [cchildren](#note26c) may know to what source they may look for a [dremission](#note26d) of their sins.

27 Wherefore, we speak concerning the law that our children may know the deadness of the law; and they, by knowing the deadness of the law, may look forward unto that life which is in Christ, and know for what end the law was given. And after the law is fulfilled in Christ, that they need not harden their hearts against him when the law ought to be done away.

28 And now behold, my people, ye are a [astiffnecked](#note28a) people; wherefore, I have spoken plainly unto you, that ye cannot misunderstand. And the words which I have spoken shall stand as a [btestimony](#note28b) against you; for they are sufficient to [cteach](#note28c) any man the [dright](#note28d) way; for the right way is to believe in Christ and deny him not; for by denying him ye also deny the prophets and the law.

29 And now behold, I say unto you that the right way is to believe in Christ, and deny him not; and Christ is the Holy One of Israel; wherefore ye must bow down before him, and [aworship](#note29a) him with all your [bmight](#note29b), mind, and strength, and your whole soul; and if ye do this ye shall in nowise be cast out.

30 And, inasmuch as it shall be expedient, ye must keep the [aperformances](#note30a) and [bordinances](#note30b) of God until the law shall be fulfilled which was given unto Moses.

Chapter 26

Christ will minister to the Nephites—Nephi foresees the destruction of his people—They will speak from the dust—The Gentiles will build up false churches and secret combinations—The Lord forbids men to practice priestcrafts. About 559–545 B.C.

1 And after Christ shall have [arisen](#note1a) from the dead he shall [bshow](#note1b) himself unto you, my children, and my beloved brethren; and the words which he shall speak unto you shall be the [claw](#note1c) which ye shall do.

2 For behold, I say unto you that I have beheld that many generations shall pass away, and there shall be great wars and contentions among my people.

3 And after the Messiah shall come there shall be [asigns](#note3a) given unto my people of his [bbirth](#note3b), and also of his [cdeath](#note3c) and resurrection; and great and terrible shall that day be unto the wicked, for they shall perish; and they perish because they cast out the [dprophets](#note3d), and the saints, and stone them, and slay them; wherefore the cry of the [eblood](#note3e) of the saints shall ascend up to God from the ground against them.

4 Wherefore, all those who are proud, and that do wickedly, the day that cometh shall [aburn](#note4a) them up, saith the Lord of Hosts, for they shall be as stubble.

5 And they that kill the [aprophets](#note5a), and the saints, the depths of the earth shall [bswallow](#note5b) them up, saith the Lord of Hosts; and [cmountains](#note5c) shall cover them, and whirlwinds shall carry them away, and buildings shall fall upon them and crush them to pieces and grind them to powder.

6 And they shall be visited with thunderings, and lightnings, and earthquakes, and all manner of destructions, for the [afire](#note6a) of the anger of the Lord shall be kindled against them, and they shall be as stubble, and the day that cometh shall consume them, saith the Lord of Hosts.

7 [aO](#note7a) the pain, and the anguish of my soul for the loss of the slain of my people! For I, Nephi, have seen it, and it well nigh consumeth me before the presence of the Lord; but I must cry unto my God: Thy ways are [bjust](#note7b).

8 But behold, the righteous that hearken unto the words of the prophets, and destroy them not, but look forward unto Christ with [asteadfastness](#note8a) for the signs which are given, notwithstanding all [bpersecution](#note8b)—behold, they are they which shall [cnot perish](#note8c).

9 But the Son of Righteousness shall [aappear](#note9a) unto them; and he shall [bheal](#note9b) them, and they shall have [cpeace](#note9c) with him, until [dthree](#note9d) generations shall have passed away, and many of the [efourth](#note9e) generation shall have passed away in righteousness.

10 And when these things have passed away a speedy [adestruction](#note10a) cometh unto my people; for, notwithstanding the pains of my soul, I have seen it; wherefore, I know that it shall come to pass; and they sell themselves for naught; for, for the reward of their pride and their [bfoolishness](#note10b) they shall reap destruction; for because they yield unto the devil and [cchoose](#note10c) works of [ddarkness](#note10d) rather than light, therefore they must go down to [ehell](#note10e).

11 For the Spirit of the Lord will not always [astrive](#note11a) with man. And when the Spirit [bceaseth](#note11b) to strive with man then cometh speedy destruction, and this grieveth my soul.

12 And as I spake concerning the [aconvincing](#note12a) of the [bJews](#note12b), that Jesus is the [cvery Christ](#note12c), it must needs be that the Gentiles be convinced also that Jesus is the Christ, the [dEternal](#note12d) [eGod](#note12e);

13 And that he [amanifesteth](#note13a) himself unto all those who believe in him, by the power of the [bHoly Ghost](#note13b); yea, unto every nation, kindred, tongue, and people, working mighty [cmiracles](#note13c), signs, and wonders, among the children of men according to their [dfaith](#note13d).

14 But behold, I prophesy unto you concerning the [alast days](#note14a); concerning the days when the Lord God shall [bbring](#note14b) these things forth unto the children of men.

15 After my seed and the seed of my brethren shall have [adwindled](#note15a) in unbelief, and shall have been smitten by the Gentiles; yea, after the Lord God shall have [bcamped](#note15b) against them round about, and shall have laid siege against them with a mount, and raised forts against them; and after they shall have been brought down low in the dust, even that they are not, yet the words of the righteous shall be written, and the [cprayers](#note15c) of the faithful shall be heard, and all those who have [ddwindled](#note15d) in unbelief shall not be forgotten.

16 For those who shall be destroyed shall [aspeak](#note16a) unto them out of the ground, and their speech shall be low out of the dust, and their voice shall be as one that hath a familiar spirit; for the Lord God will give unto him power, that he may whisper concerning them, even as it were out of the ground; and their speech shall whisper out of the dust.

17 For thus saith the Lord God: They shall [awrite](#note17a) the things which shall be done among them, and they shall be written and [bsealed](#note17b) up in a book, and those who have dwindled in [cunbelief](#note17c) shall not have them, for they [dseek](#note17d) to destroy the things of God.

18 Wherefore, as those who have been destroyed have been destroyed speedily; and the multitude of their [aterrible ones](#note18a) shall be as [bchaff](#note18b) that passeth away—yea, thus saith the Lord God: It shall be at an instant, suddenly—

19 And it shall come to pass, that those who have dwindled in unbelief shall be [asmitten](#note19a) by the hand of the Gentiles.

20 And the Gentiles are lifted up in the [apride](#note20a) of their eyes, and have [bstumbled](#note20b), because of the greatness of their [cstumbling block](#note20c), that they have built up many [dchurches](#note20d); nevertheless, they [eput down](#note20e) the power and miracles of God, and preach up unto themselves their own wisdom and their own [flearning](#note20f), that they may get gain and [ggrind](#note20g) upon the face of the poor.

21 And there are many churches built up which cause [aenvyings](#note21a), and [bstrifes](#note21b), and [cmalice](#note21c).

22 And there are also secret [acombinations](#note22a), even as in times of old, according to the combinations of the [bdevil](#note22b), for he is the founder of all these things; yea, the founder of murder, and [cworks](#note22c) of darkness; yea, and he leadeth them by the neck with a flaxen cord, until he bindeth them with his strong cords forever.

23 For behold, my beloved brethren, I say unto you that the Lord God worketh not in [adarkness](#note23a).

24 He doeth not [aanything](#note24a) save it be for the benefit of the world; for he [bloveth](#note24b) the world, even that he layeth down his own life that he may draw [call](#note24c) men unto him. Wherefore, he commandeth none that they shall not partake of his salvation.

25 Behold, doth he cry unto any, saying: Depart from me? Behold, I say unto you, Nay; but he saith: [aCome](#note25a) unto me all ye [bends](#note25b) of the earth, [cbuy](#note25c) milk and honey, without money and without price.

26 Behold, hath he commanded any that they should [adepart](#note26a) out of the synagogues, or out of the houses of worship? Behold, I say unto you, Nay.

27 Hath he commanded any that they should not partake of his [asalvation](#note27a)? Behold I say unto you, Nay; but he hath [bgiven](#note27b) it free for all men; and he hath commanded his people that they should persuade all men to [crepentance](#note27c).

28 Behold, hath the Lord commanded any that they should not partake of his goodness? Behold I say unto you, Nay; but [aall](#note28a) men are privileged the one [blike](#note28b) unto the other, and none are forbidden.

29 He commandeth that there shall be no [apriestcrafts](#note29a); for, behold, priestcrafts are that men preach and set [bthemselves](#note29b) up for a light unto the world, that they may get [cgain](#note29c) and [dpraise](#note29d) of the world; but they seek not the [ewelfare](#note29e) of Zion.

30 Behold, the Lord hath forbidden this thing; wherefore, the Lord God hath given a commandment that all men should have [acharity](#note30a), which [bcharity](#note30b) is [clove](#note30c). And except they should have charity they were nothing. Wherefore, if they should have charity they would not suffer the laborer in Zion to perish.

31 But the [alaborer](#note31a) in [bZion](#note31b) shall labor for Zion; for if they labor for [cmoney](#note31c) they shall perish.

32 And again, the Lord God hath [acommanded](#note32a) that men should not murder; that they should not lie; that they should not [bsteal](#note32b); that they should not take the name of the Lord their God in [cvain](#note32c); that they should not [denvy](#note32d); that they should not have [emalice](#note32e); that they should not contend one with another; that they should not commit [fwhoredoms](#note32f); and that they should do none of these things; for whoso doeth them shall perish.

33 For none of these iniquities come of the Lord; for he doeth that which is good among the children of men; and he doeth nothing save it be plain unto the children of men; and he [ainviteth](#note33a) them [ball](#note33b) to [ccome](#note33c) unto him and partake of his goodness; and he [ddenieth](#note33d) none that come unto him, black and white, [ebond](#note33e) and free, male and female; and he remembereth the [fheathen](#note33f); and all are alike unto God, both Jew and Gentile.

Chapter 27

Darkness and apostasy will cover the earth in the last days—The Book of Mormon will come forth—Three witnesses will testify of the book—The learned man will say he cannot read the sealed book—The Lord will do a marvelous work and a wonder—Compare Isaiah 29. About 559–545 B.C.

1 But, behold, in the [alast days](#note1a), or in the days of the Gentiles—yea, behold all the nations of the Gentiles and also the Jews, both those who shall come upon this land and those who shall be upon other lands, yea, even upon all the lands of the earth, behold, they will be [bdrunken](#note1b) with iniquity and all manner of abominations—

2 And when that day shall come they shall be [avisited](#note2a) of the Lord of Hosts, with thunder and with earthquake, and with a great noise, and with storm, and with tempest, and with the [bflame](#note2b) of devouring fire.

3 And all the [anations](#note3a) that [bfight](#note3b) against Zion, and that distress her, shall be as a dream of a night vision; yea, it shall be unto them, even as unto a hungry man which dreameth, and behold he eateth but he awaketh and his soul is empty; or like unto a thirsty man which dreameth, and behold he drinketh but he awaketh and behold he is faint, and his soul hath appetite; yea, even so shall the multitude of all the nations be that fight against Mount Zion.

4 For behold, all ye that doeth iniquity, stay yourselves and wonder, for ye shall cry out, and cry; yea, ye shall be [adrunken](#note4a) but not with wine, ye shall stagger but not with strong drink.

5 For behold, the Lord hath poured out upon you the spirit of deep sleep. For behold, ye have closed your [aeyes](#note5a), and ye have [brejected](#note5b) the prophets; and your rulers, and the seers hath he covered because of your iniquity.

6 And it shall come to pass that the Lord God shall bring forth unto [ayou](#note6a) the words of a [bbook](#note6b), and they shall be the words of them which have slumbered.

7 And behold the book shall be [asealed](#note7a); and in the book shall be a [brevelation](#note7b) from God, from the beginning of the world to the [cending](#note7c) thereof.

8 Wherefore, because of the things which are [asealed](#note8a) up, the things which are sealed shall not be delivered in the day of the wickedness and abominations of the people. Wherefore the book shall be kept from them.

9 But the book shall be delivered unto a man, and he shall deliver the words of the book, which are the words of those who have slumbered in the dust, and he shall deliver these words unto [aanother](#note9a);

10 But the words which are [asealed](#note10a) he shall not deliver, neither shall he deliver the book. For the book shall be sealed by the power of God, and the revelation which was sealed shall be kept in the book until the own due time of the Lord, that they may come forth; for behold, they [breveal](#note10b) all things from the foundation of the world unto the end thereof.

11 And the day cometh that the words of the book which were sealed shall be read upon the house tops; and they shall be read by the power of Christ; and all things shall be [arevealed](#note11a) unto the children of men which ever have been among the children of men, and which ever will be even unto the end of the earth.

12 Wherefore, at that day when the book shall be delivered unto the man of whom I have spoken, the book shall be hid from the eyes of the world, that the eyes of none shall behold it save it be that [athree](#note12a) [bwitnesses](#note12b) shall behold it, by the power of God, besides him to whom the book shall be delivered; and they shall testify to the truth of the book and the things therein.

13 And there is [anone](#note13a) other which shall view it, save it be a few according to the will of God, to bear testimony of his word unto the children of men; for the Lord God hath said that the words of the faithful should speak as if it were [bfrom the dead](#note13b).

14 Wherefore, the Lord God will proceed to bring forth the words of the book; and in the mouth of as many witnesses as seemeth him good will he establish his word; and wo be unto him that [arejecteth](#note14a) the word of God!

15 But behold, it shall come to pass that the Lord God shall say unto him to whom he shall deliver the book: Take these words which are not sealed and deliver them to another, that he may show them unto the learned, saying: [aRead](#note15a) this, I pray thee. And the learned shall say: Bring hither the book, and I will read them.

16 And now, because of the glory of the world and to get [again](#note16a) will they say this, and not for the glory of God.

17 And the man shall say: I cannot bring the book, for it is sealed.

18 Then shall the learned say: I cannot read it.

19 Wherefore it shall come to pass, that the Lord God will [adeliver](#note19a) again the book and the words thereof to him that is not learned; and the man that is not learned shall say: I am not learned.

20 Then shall the Lord God say unto him: The learned shall not read them, for they have rejected them, and I am [aable](#note20a) to do mine own work; wherefore thou shalt read the words which I shall give unto thee.

21 [aTouch not](#note21a) the things which are sealed, for I will bring them forth in mine own due time; for I will show unto the children of men that I am able to do mine own work.

22 Wherefore, when thou hast read the words which I have commanded thee, and obtained the [awitnesses](#note22a) which I have promised unto thee, then shalt thou seal up the book again, and hide it up unto me, that I may preserve the words which thou hast not read, until I shall see fit in mine own [bwisdom](#note22b) to [creveal](#note22c) all things unto the children of men.

23 For behold, I am God; and I am a God of [amiracles](#note23a); and I will show unto the [bworld](#note23b) that I am the same yesterday, today, and forever; and I [cwork](#note23c) not among the children of men save it be [daccording](#note23d) to their faith.

24 And again it shall come to pass that the Lord shall say unto him that shall read the words that shall be delivered him:

25 [aForasmuch](#note25a) as this people draw near unto me with their mouth, and with their lips do [bhonor](#note25b) me, but have removed their [chearts](#note25c) far from me, and their fear towards me is taught by the [dprecepts](#note25d) of men—

26 Therefore, I will proceed to do a [amarvelous work](#note26a) among this people, yea, a [bmarvelous work](#note26b) and a wonder, for the [cwisdom](#note26c) of their wise and [dlearned](#note26d) shall perish, and the [eunderstanding](#note26e) of their [fprudent](#note26f) shall be hid.

27 And [awo](#note27a) unto them that seek deep to hide their [bcounsel](#note27b) from the Lord! And their works are in the [cdark](#note27c); and they say: Who seeth us, and who knoweth us? And they also say: Surely, your turning of things upside down shall be esteemed as the [dpotter’s](#note27d) clay. But behold, I will show unto them, saith the Lord of Hosts, that I [eknow](#note27e) all their works. For shall the work say of him that made it, he made me not? Or shall the thing framed say of him that framed it, he had no understanding?

28 But behold, saith the Lord of Hosts: I will show unto the children of men that it is yet a very little while and Lebanon shall be turned into a fruitful field; and the [afruitful](#note28a) field shall be esteemed as a forest.

29 [aAnd](#note29a) in that day shall the [bdeaf](#note29b) hear the words of the book, and the eyes of the blind shall see out of obscurity and out of darkness.

30 And the [ameek](#note30a) also shall increase, and their [bjoy](#note30b) shall be in the Lord, and the poor among men shall rejoice in the Holy One of Israel.

31 For assuredly as the Lord liveth they shall see that the [aterrible one](#note31a) is brought to naught, and the scorner is consumed, and all that watch for iniquity are cut off;

32 And they that make a man an [aoffender](#note32a) for a word, and lay a snare for him that reproveth in the [bgate](#note32b), and [cturn](#note32c) aside the just for a thing of naught.

33 Therefore, thus saith the Lord, who redeemed Abraham, concerning the house of Jacob: Jacob shall [anot now](#note33a) be ashamed, neither shall his face now wax pale.

34 But when he [aseeth](#note34a) his children, the work of my hands, in the midst of him, they shall sanctify my name, and sanctify the Holy One of Jacob, and shall fear the God of Israel.

35 They also that [aerred](#note35a) in spirit shall come to understanding, and they that murmured shall [blearn](#note35b) doctrine.
